CONFIDENTIAL

FORTNIGHTLY INTELLIGENCE REPORT NO. 13.

Far Eastern Bureau,
British Ministry of Information,
New Delhi.

Period ended
September 11th, 1943.

MALAYA AND SUMATRA.

POLITICAL.

1. Ibrahim bin Haji Yacob: The Japanese have been acclaiming Ibrahim bin Haji Yacob, head of the "Malayan Inspection Party" visiting Japan. (See F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra, No. 7, para 10; No. 10, para 3; No. 12 paras 5 and 6.) According to an account by Domei Ibrahim "organized the young nationalists in Malaya about 10 years ago into the Malayan Young Men's League under the cloak of its being a cultural body." In due course he came into contact with Michio Hirakawa, then "the centre of a certain Japanese Intelligence organ" in Malaya, and was convinced by him that only Japan could be the leader of Asia. Hirakawa "obtained strong backing" for the Malayan Young Men's League and it was "converted into an active secret society." Later the League bought the Warta Melayu and Ibrahim became President of the paper. Able members of the League were appointed to posts in branches of this newspaper all over Malaya. By this means "all kinds of intelligence about the disposition of defence workers of British troops, such as landing spots in Kota Bharu, fortifications on the Perak River, and the stronghold in Klang were collected." When the Japanese attacked Malaya Ibrahim was imprisoned and Hirakawa interned in India. The Japanese appointed Ibrahim to "a post in the Marine Administration Office" where he has "devoted himself to the welfare of his brethren and has thus won the respect of his fellow countrymen." Hirakawa returned to Japan by the exchange ship from India. Ibrahim stated publicly in Tokyo that events had proved that his aim in starting the Malayan Young Men's League in 1930 "was completely right", and that while in Japan he intended to "study the conditions of youth education." (Domei in Japanese, August 16th).

2. Tengku Hussain on the ceding of the four Northern States to Siam: Tengku Hussain declared that "the incorporation of Kedah, Perlis, Kelantan, and Trengganu into Thai territory means a reunion of Thais and Malays whose historical relationship had never been severed until British Imperialism" interfered. Referring to Trengganu he said that as inter-marriage between the two nations had been going on for a long time, many Malays of Trengganu were of Siamese descent, and that Malays are not foreign to Siam, thousands of them enjoying privileges under the Siamese Peoples Constitution. (Domei in English, September 7th). Comment: Tengku Hussain is a grandson of the late Sultan Ali, the last Sultan of Singapore. He is about 30 years old and is married to a cousin of the present Sultan of Trengganu. He received two pensions, one from the Straits Settlement Government and one from Trengganu. He also married a Kelantan girl which led to his leaving Trengganu and his Trengganu wife for some time. (See F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra, No. 9, para 1, and Appendices I to IV). Tengku Hussain and Japanese propagandists are incorrect in implying that the Siamese represent any material proportion of the populations of the ceded Malay States. The percentage of people of Siamese origin in these States is: Kedah 2.96%, Perlis 2.44%, Kelantan 2.13%, and in Trengganu 0.02%.

===== Page 58 =====
3. Self-protection Corps and Neighbourhood Associations, Malacca: S. Tanaka, head of the Publicity Department, has been touring the Kampongs of Malacca to "strengthen the two most useful public organisations, the Self-protection Corps and Neighbourhood Associations." Tanaka's theme is 'mass-discipline'. (Domei in English, September 4th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.9 para 15.

4. The Heiho (Auxiliary Service Corps): Malays, Chinese, Indians, and Eurasians in Kedah are eagerly joining the Heiho and undergoing their training. Malay girls in Kedah are "exhibiting the same spirit." (Domei in English, September 6th). The party of eight Singapore journalists who left on a tour of Western Malaya on August 16th reported, upon their return to Singapore, that they were 'struck by the rigorous training and discipline of Heiho recruits in the Ipoh region.' (Domei in English, August 31st). See F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.8, para 6.

5. Neighbourhood Corps: Rinpohan (Neighbourhood Corps) have been formed primarily to undertake A.R.P. and passive defence duties. (Domei in English, September 3rd).

6. Police Officers: 147 Police Officers, graduates of the Police School of the Malaya Military Administration, are leaving shortly to take up their police duties. (Domei in English, September 1st).

7. Police Certificates of Merit: 7 Police Officers have been awarded certificates of merit by Shotaro Katayama, Governor of Selangor. (Domei in English, September 10th).

8. I.I.L.- Subhas Chandra Bose: Addressing Singapore Naval Base workers, Subhas Chandra Bose expressed appreciation of their spirit of nationalism and warned them against "the un-Indian activity of certain undesirable elements." (Domei in English, August 28th). Addressing a meeting of 15,000 members of the I.I.L., before the Penang Broadcasting Station, S.C. Bose said that Indians were depending upon Japan's whole-hearted support in the present movement towards independence and added, "In the near future we shall see Indians marching across the frontier on to Delhi with the flag of independence." He said that it was important to form a "provisional government of Indians." Indians present are declared to have shown their "desire to overthrow the Anglo-American yoke" by a donation of $2,000,000. In Taiping, Perak, Indians presented Bose with a purse of $20,000 for the liberation of India and a body of 165 Perak Indian youths left to join the Indian National Army in Singapore. At Ipoh, Bose told Indians, "We must contribute our total man-power in ousting the British from India." (Domei in English, September 7th and 9th). Bose spoke to 50,000 Indians at Kuala Lumpur, in front of the Selangor Government offices, where some enlisted in the Azad Hind Army in Singapore and others made contributions amounting to $2,000,000. (Domei in English, September 7th).

9. I.I.L.- Sumatra: Medan: The Governor of the East Coast of Sumatra, Japanese Officials and Residents "from other parts of East Asia" attended the first anniversary meeting of the I.I.L. L.T. Maharani, President of the local branch "urged Indians to unite for the cause of the Mother Land." (Nanpo Domei, September 9th).

10. S.C. Bose's Appeal to Women: At Penang, in a speech appealing to Indian women to support the movement for independence, Bose said: "Our women are also going into

===== Page 59 =====
battle." (Domei in English, September 8th). The women's section of the I.I.L. presented him with more than ¥7,000. (Domei in English, September 8th).

11. Dr. Lakshmi at Johore Bahru: Speaking to 800 Indian women at Johore Bahru, Dr. Lakshmi said that "our Indian brothers... will expect great things of the Jhansi Regiment. We will not fail them." "At the conclusion of her speech, many young women volunteered to join the Regiment." (Domei in English, August 28th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.11 para 9.

12. I.I.L.: Contributions of Penang Muslims: Penang Muslim leaders have "pledged a sum of ¥60,000 with further sums to be collected." (Domei in English, September 7th).

18. Azad Hind Training Camp: The Azad Hind Training Camp for Indian National Army volunteers will be officially opened in Singapore on September 3rd. It will be the largest of such Camps in Malaya, there being "hundreds of part-time training centres scattered over the country." Another Camp is to be opened in Seremban shortly. (Domei in English, September 24th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.8, para 12. During the last month, more than 500 Indian volunteers have received training for the Indian National Army. (Domei in English, September 2nd).

ECONOMIC.

14. Increase of Inter-regional Remittances: "Reflecting the increase of inter-regional trade in East Asia," remittances from Malaya to Burma, Sumatra, Java, North Borneo and the Philippines have increased monthly. The remittances were as follows:

March 22 remittances totalling 250,000 yen;
April 41 " 286,000 ";
May 82 " 2,478,000 ";
June 402 " 6,758,000 ";
July 1,261 " 7,213,000 ";
August 978 " 8,835,000 ".

(Domei in English, September 5th). Comment: Malaya's total value of merchandise imported from and exported to the Netherlands Indies alone was ¥220,054,000 in 1937.

15. Yokohama Specie Bank, Kuantan Branch: The Yokohama Specie Bank has opened a branch at Kuantan on September 1st. "This is the second branch of the Bank to be opened in Pahang." (Domei in English, September 4th). Comment: Presumably the other branch is at Kuala Lipis. Before the Japanese invasion the Mercantile Bank of India had branches at Kuala Lipis and Kuantan.

16. The Kwong Yik Bank and Southern Regions Bank: Kuala Lumpur: The Kwong Yik Bank is to reopen at Kuala Lumpur on September 1st. It will be the sixth bank to re-operate in Selangor. The Southern Regions Bank is shortly opening a branch office at Kuala Lumpur. (Domei in English, August 21st).

===== Page 60 =====
17. Family Remittances to China: Since they were first permitted in April, remittances by Malayan Chinese to their families in China have continued to increase. Remittances, at a permitted maximum of ¥100 per month per head, were ¥12,000 in April and ¥97,000 in August. (Domei in English, September 3rd). 8,124 transfers have been effected, amounting to ¥332,866. (C.P.D. Monitoring, Batavia in English, August 29/30; 1130 GMT, 16.6m; Domei in English, August 28th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.2 para 13; No.6 paras 17 & 18.

18. Savings Campaign: All member-banks of the Malayan Banking Association will receive savings from the public and grant 3% interest on fixed deposits and 2% for ordinary savings. (Domei in English, September 2nd). Singapore banks reported a good response from the public during the week's savings campaign. (Domei in English, September 10th). August was a record month for postal savings in Penang with a total deposit of ¥30,000 in the Post Office Savings Bank. (Domei in English, September 7th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra, No.10 para 17.

19. Onan bin Haji Siraj: Onan bin Haji Siraj, a director of the local Malay farms, Singapore, has been awarded a certificate of merit by the Director-General of Posts for his promotion of thrift among Malay farmers. (Domei in English, September 4th). See F.I.R. No.11 Malaya and Sumatra para 14.

20. First Harvest of Taiwan Rice in Kedah: Seiji Sukekawa, Governor of Kedah, helped rice growers to reap the first harvest of Taiwan rice which he had helped them to plant. A party of Singapore journalists (see F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.3, App.1, para 21 & 22) sampled this rice at the Governor's dinner. (Domei in English, August 30th).

21. Perak Experimental Rice Growing: The trial planting farm covering 1,300 se in Perak is producing an average crop of 2,400 tons of Taiwan rice per se (7 se = approximately 1 acre) and 1,500 lbs of Malayan rice per se. This is twice as much per se as before the war. Trial planting on a still larger scale will begin early in September. (Domei in English, September 1st).

22. Medan: Co-operative Vegetable Gardening: The newly created government employees' co-operative societies have been granted ground for the cultivation of vegetables. (Nanpo Domei, September 9th).

23. Cultivation of Idle lands: The employees of the Toyo Kazan Kabushiki Kaisha are cultivating idle land in Taiping. All members of the staff, including Japanese, work in the fields cultivating maize, padi, tapioca and other plants every weekend. (Domei in English, August 30th).

24. Food Self-sufficiency: Three Singapore hospitals are supplying their own meat and vegetables after successful experiments in vegetable growing and pig rearing. Municipal hospitals all over the country expect to have their own farms for the production of foodstuffs. (Domei in English, August 26th). Indians and Chinese in Kuala Lumpur are reported to be rearing rabbits for food. (Domei in English, September 6th). Comment: Most pork consumed in Malaya came from Siam and Banka, while the beef came from Australia, New Zealand and Bali and the mutton and lamb from Australia and New Zealand.

===== Page 61 =====
25. Johore Exports Foodstuffs to Singapore: "Johore has attained self-sufficiency in the majority of foodstuffs" and is exporting her surplus vegetables, maize, tapioca, sweet-potatoes and yams in abundance to Singapore. (Domei in English, September 3rd.)

26. Farm Implements at Special Rates to Farmers in Sumatra: Farm implements are being supplied for the production of foodstuffs at special rates. (Domei in English, September 1st).

27. Sungei Manik: Perak Indians have cleared 900 acres of land in the Sungei Manik area allotted to them for the cultivation of foodstuffs. (Domei in English, August 30th). See F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No. 11 para 18.

28. Singapore Island Agriculture: The agriculture and forestry department of the Special Municipality have stated that the acreage under food production has been increased from 1,500 acres before the invasion to 4,500 in March 1943 and that it is to be further increased to 5,700. Chinese squatters have increased from 6,707 to 34,504 and Malay squatters are now approximately 500. The Overseas-Chinese Association and the Neighbourhood Associations are encouraging food production. (Domei in English, September 4th). Comment: There is only limited suitable land for market gardening on Singapore Island as in general all land not under forest has been seriously damaged by erosion. If the Japanese are prepared to permit the felling of the few remaining jungle areas they will have no shortage of Chinese willing to reap the first few rich crops obtainable from newly-felled areas.

29. Chinese Settlement at Puchong: Selangor: The first twenty-five Chinese families have settled in the newly-cleared settlement of 1,800 acres of forest land earmarked for food cultivation at Puchong. Half the land has been cleared and when the rest is ready for cultivation, the Overseas-Chinese Association will send further settlers. (Domei in English, September 2nd). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No. 2 para 17; No. 7 para 16.

30. Proposed Agricultural Settlement in Negri Sembilan: "70,000 acres of a proposed area of 90,000 acres" have been cleared in Negri Sembilan for a new agricultural settlement. Settlers have been established there on Government subsidies granted in the form of farm implements, irrigation schemes, technical advice, importation of farm labour and buffaloes and seeds and the furnishing of medical advice. "Already 2,000 acres are under Taiwan rice and in the Kuala Pilah and Rembau areas 20,000 coconut seedlings have been planted." Malay operas, cinemas and musical plays have been provided. (Domei in English, September 6th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No. 2 para 19.

31. Condensed Milk for Singapore: "Condensed milk is now sold in bottles at a reasonable price by a number of farms and dispensaries and provides a supply of rich and healthy milk ... The industry is past the experimental stage and has secured for itself a good position on the market." (Domei in English, September 7th). See F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No. 11 para 20; No. 8 para 14. Comment: The Japanese appear to be on the defensive in their propaganda regarding milk, the shortage of which in Malaya is a serious problem.

===== Page 62 =====
32. Castor Bean: Castor beans are being supplied free of charge to Chinese farmers to assist them in their cultivation of the plant. (Domei in English, September 8th).

33. Fibre: Superior ramie plants are being imported into Sumatra for large-scale planting. Cultivation of pineapple and palm fibres is increasing. "Fibre spinning and weaving factories are now in operation in various localities." (Domei in English, August 31st).

34. Key Industrial Goods Control Act: The military administration of Sumatra has passed a Key Industries Goods Act empowering the military administration to issue orders (i) to restrict or prohibit the transfer, loan, use, consumption or disposition and receipt of important commodities, plants, equipment facilities, land, buildings, etc.; (ii) to utilize or requisition the above goods or production factors; (iii) to transfer or dispose of the items specified above by fixing terms and conditions; (iv) to collect reports and data and inspect businesses and materials as required. The Act has been promulgated "to increase fighting power by controlling supply and demand for raw materials, etc., and to conserve goods." (Domei in English, September 8th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.11 para 24.

35. Production Materials Control Act: The military administration "are now going to stress good organisation" (i) to secure public peace; (ii) "to develop and send home important materials for national defence", and (iii) to encourage "self-support in munitions by fostering and promoting industry on the scene". Industries will be graded according to importance and allotted "installations and properties according to priority ... no machines and property being left idle". This "will be strictly enforced and a strict penal code is to be enacted against offenders". (Domei in Japanese, August 28th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra, No.11 para 24.

36. Negri Sembilan Industries: Factories have been opened in Negri Sembilan for the making of nails, axes, shovels, ropes, canvas and other agricultural implements. (Domei in English, September 2nd).

37. Singapore Sample Fair: There will be a display of various locally-produced articles at the Great World, Singapore, in mid-September. Articles exhibited will include fibre goods, rubber and agricultural products, health and sanitation exhibits, etc. (Domei in English, August 28th). There is to be a "Self-sufficiency Encouragement Hall" 100 ft. x 32 ft. which "will include a typical Japanese tea-house". The exhibits will include hundreds of pictures portraying various phases of Japanese culture. (Domei in English, September 7th). Comment: The Great World was one of the Singapore "Amusement Parks".

38. Shozo Murata: Murata, Adviser to the Japanese Military administration in the Philippines, has made an extensive inspection trip of Sumatra. He remarked upon "the complete peace and order throughout Sumatra and the progress made in agriculture and industry." He was surprised at the rich resources of the Island and thought that its speedy development "will be an immense contribution to the welfare of the people of East Asia." (C.P.D. monitoring, Tokyo in English August 28th/29th, 940 GMT, 19.86 m.). Murata left for Saigon on September 1st to continue "his inspection tour of the Southern Regions." (Domei in English, September 1st). Comment: Shozo Murata was president of the Osaka

===== Page 63 =====
Shosen Kaisha and an Imperial nominee in the House of Peers in 1939. He used to be President of the Japan-America Society in Kansai and a director of the Japan Broadcasting Corporation. He was chairman of seven shipping, industrial, and chemical concerns and an adviser of the Osaka Chamber of Commerce and Industry and chairman of the Japan Shipowners' Association.

39. Pottery: "The Selangor earthenware industry is enjoying an unprecedented boom," (Domei in English, August 28th). Comment: Pottery has been a neglected industry in Malaya. In 1937 there were eight pottery factories on Singapore Island, outside the Singapore municipal area, one in Penang and one in Malacca. The articles most commonly made in Malaya were water-bottles, water jars, cooking pots, incense burners, steam cookers, drinking cups, small plates, and the like. Most vessels used in Malaya were imported from Swatow. Articles of crude porcelain from China were so cheap that they displaced the local pottery. Excellent Kaolin is found in Johore in the Kluang area.

40. Nipah: "Hundreds of Malay and Chinese women and children" are engaged in drying nipah leaves in the Pasir Panjang area of Singapore. The leaves are sold for making cigarettes. (Domei in English, August 31st). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.12 para. Comment: Nipah leaves have long been used for wrapping native Malay tobacco, but imported cigarettes were ousting the local product. Doubtless the industry has revived with the isolation of Malaya from imported tobacco.

41. Local Oils as Lubricants: Coconut palm and vegetable oils are being used in the production of lubricating oil. The Materials Utilisation Committee in collaboration with the Railway Bureau, the Showa Rubber Company, and the Mitsui Bussan Kaisha have conducted successful tests for substitutes for mineral oil. (Domei in English, September 2nd). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.2 para 27; No.3 para 19; No.12 para 19.

42. Cassia Mata: Cure for Malaria: Domei reports that a Medan doctor has discovered "an effective new cure for Malaria". The medicine is a concoction from the cassia mata plant plentiful in Sumatra and Malaya. (Domei in English, September 1st). Comment: Cassia is the genus of trees, shrubs, and herbs of the family leguminosae. These plants contain emodin and allied glucosides, some chrysophanic acids, and tannin. Their chief medicinal use is as an aperient and for skin troubles. No mention can be found of their having alkaloid and anti-febrile properties.

43. Nankoh Shokai: This company, run by "Matsuo of the Department of Commerce and Industry" are authorised distributors of Japanese goods in Selangor. (Domei in English, August 28th). See F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.9 para 27; No.11 para 27.

44. Hydro-electric Power in Perak: The Nippon Power Generation and Transmission Company's Malayan branch is investigating two sites in Perak for the establishment of hydro-electric power plants. The proposed new plants are intended to take over the work of the "two coal power electric plants in the vicinity, thus effecting saving of coal". (Domei in English, September 7th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra No.8 para 36. Comment: The coal plants referred to are doubtless the Perak River Hydro-electric Power Company's two steam-electric installations in the Kinta valley.

===== Page 64 =====
45. Port Dickson Harbour: Kin, District Officer, Port Dickson, has stressed the value of Port Dickson as a regular port of call for local ships plying along the west coast of Malaya. It is expected that the work of enlarging the harbour and providing it with excellent shipping facilities will be completed within the next three years. (Domei in English, September 2nd). Comment: Port Dickson is a pretty holiday resort with good beaches in a bay on the coast of Negri Sembilan. It was the headquarters of the Malay Regiment. Basket-weaving and fishing were the chief industries. Kin is most probably a Korean but may be a Formosan or even a Japanese.

46. English Language Ban in Sumatra: There is a ban on the use of English "in Malay matters" and the authorities at Bukit Tinggi (Fort de Kock) have prohibited the use of English in long distance telephone calls and telegrams. (Domei in English, September 2nd). Comment: English was so very little used in Sumatra that this will affect few persons.

47. Express Postal Service: On September 10th an express delivery service for all except parcels was instituted at Singapore, Johore Bahru, Malacca, Seremban, Kuala Lumpur, Kuala Lipis, Ipoh, Taiping and Penang. (Domei in English, September 10th).

48. Commemoration Stamps: All Post Offices in Malaya will sell special Commemoration Stamps of 8 and 15 cent denominations during "commemoration week" beginning September 1st. A special date stamp will be used. (Domei in English; August 30th). See also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra, No.12 para 11.

49. Unified Control of Broadcasting: The programmes of the Penang, Kuala Lumpur and Singapore Broadcasting Stations will be under unified control as from September 17th. The power of the Kuala Lumpur station has been increased so that it may "play a vital role in the radio network of the peninsula". (Domei in English, September 4th).

50. Motor-car Regulations: Regulations have been promulgated prohibiting the transfer or loan of automobiles or parts without a permit. The object is "the economic use of the available automobiles". (Domei in English, August 28th).

SOCIAL AND CULTURAL.

51. Public Welfare Conference, Malacca: Ken Tsurumi, Governor of Malacca, presided at a conference of local community leaders and officials 'to discuss important matters affecting the general welfare of the public'. It was decided that 'no destitution or unemployment should prevail in the State'. (Domei in English, September 7th).

52. Singapore Street Signs: All street signs in Singapore are in katakana. (Batavia in English, September 5th, 1030 GMT, 16.54 m.).

53. Malayan Officers' Training Institute: The third batch of students consisting of Malays, Chinese, Indians and Filipinos (sic) from 17 to 25 years of age, "from the Selangor area" have gone to the Malayan Officers' Training Institute for training as "competent future leaders". The Officers' Training Institute (Koa Kunrenjo) with 85 students is in Malacca and trains teachers on Japanese lines.

===== Page 65 =====
54. Seremban Royal House: One of the sons of the Yang Di-Pertuan Besar of Negri Sembilan has graduated from the Officers' Training School (Kunrenjo). Hatta, the Governor of Negri Sembilan, lecturing to graduates of the school, remarked that "Rajas are treated like the other students" during the course.

55. Teachers Training Institute: 17 Malays, 17 Chinese, 8 Indians, and 3 Europeans (of whom 16 are women) successfully passed the matriculation examination for the Teachers' Training Institute held in Penang on August 22nd. "Special training classes will begin on August 22nd" (Domei in English; August 30th, September 3rd, and see also F.I.R. Malaya and Sumatra, No.10, para 37; No.8 para 44).

56. Wan Abdul Hamid bin Dato Salleh of Johore: Wan Abdul Hamid, aged 20, one of the five Malay students studying in Japan under the hospitality of Marquis Yoshichika Tokugawa, is reported to "feel at home" in Japan. He is studying agriculture with a view to "instructing his people in Japanese methods of cultivation." (Domei in English, August 30th. See also F.I.R. No.11, para 32).

57. Farmers' Training Institute at Tandjoeng Goenoeng: The first class consists of 103 students undergoing rigorous physical training on military lines under five Indonesian and some Japanese teachers. The school is run on the lines of the Uchihara Training Institute and graduates are to return to their native places to guide local cultivators. The governors of Medan, Langkat, "and other prominent figures" attended the opening of this Institute. (Nanpo Domei, September 9th). Comment: Tandjoeng Goenoeng is 40 miles from Medan.

58. Training Centre of Sumatra Youth Association: A Medan branch of this Association is to be opened as a training centre for selected youths to undergo a special three months' course 'to make them better understand Japan's ideals and the significance of the Great East Asia Co-prosperity Sphere'. (Domei in English, September 1st).

59. Alms during the fasting month: Sheik Haji Ali Mohamed Shaki, the Chief Kathi, "has announced" that the Japanese have given free rice, salt, and sugar for the fasting month. "Formerly under the British regime these rations had to be purchased out of Mosque funds or from collections raised among the Muslims." The food is intended for the poor and destitute and for strangers calling at the mosque to break their fast. (Domei in English, August 28th; C.P.D. August 29th/30th Tokyo in English, 0940 GMT. 19.86 m. and Domei in English, August 30th).

60. Singapore Mosques: All Singapore mosques have been packed every evening with Muslims assembled for the prayers known as Sembayang Teraweh. (Domei in English, September 8th). Comment: These are special prayers, taking about half an hour, made at night during the fasting month of Ramadan.

61. 22nd Anniversary of the death of Subrahmani Bharati: On September 11th, prominent members of the Tamil community in Singapore will deliver speeches on the life of the Tamil poet, patriot, and writer, Subrahmani Bharati. (Batavia in English, 1030 GMT. 16.54 m.)

62. Radio Callisthenics: Radio callisthenics have been introduced in Malaya and daily "thousands carry out these exercises in the privacy of their homes or like children, policemen, government employees in large numbers in the open." (Domei in English, September 8th).

===== Page 66 =====
