APPENDIX I

Note on British Forest Policy in Malaya

by Major Colin Marshall, Malayan Forest Service.

The object of this policy is to ensure that Malaya shall have enough timber and firewood for its internal needs and in addition shall, if possible (but it is not essential), have enough timber to support the small export trade to parts of the world, and especially an empire, which are deficient in timber resources.

The jungles of Malaya contain approximately 2,500 different species, of which some 150 are common. There are no pure stands of trees except in the mangrove forests. Many of these species are of no use either as timber or firewood.

If exploitation were permitted under normal methods without restrictions, the timber cutters would remove the best species first, and the space left vacant would be filled by the seeds and seedlings of the less valuable remaining species. The object of the forest department is to increase the proportion of valuable trees in the forest. This it does by licensing the cutting of timber so that the less valuable species are cut first. Thus, the resulting young crop contains a higher proportion of seedlings of the more valuable species. Where it is not possible to find a market for the less valuable species, these are killed by departmental labour gangs who poison the trees with sodium arsenate.

At the same time, the forest department collects revenue for the Government by charging royalty on all timber cut. The principle is that all trees growing on the ground were produced originally by Nature and that they therefore belong to the country as a whole. The occupier of the ground has therefore to pay the general community (Government) a certain percentage of any sum he may receive when selling the timber. This is royalty.

Trees do not come to maturity in a short time, and in order to ensure that there shall be a sufficient supply of timber it is necessary to cut the same volume of timber which naturally comes from this same area and is grown in each year. Thus, if a tree takes 100 years to reach commercial maturity, the forest in which that tree is growing will be divided into 100 parts, and each part, when clear of trees, will be replanted unless natural seedlings develop. This process will continue until the felting cycle comes round to that area again, by which time, of course, trees of that area will be 100 years old. In Malaya, maturity varies from 40 years to 130 years, according to the species. The forest department has for many years been developing a complete series of age gradations. It is very easy for the Japanese to produce large quantities of timber by cutting without considering the future crop, but the people will pay dearly for this in the years to come.

The policy of exploitation might change the climate of Malaya, and cause the silting up of the rivers with consequent floods, loss of life, etc. The Northern Sahara, the areas around the Euphrates head-waters, and numerous other desert areas are the result of interruption of the natural vegetation. It would take at least one hundred years to reproduce trees over an area which had been subject to devastating exploitation for a period of 10 years.

===== Page 125 =====
Union of South Africa Censorship

MEMORANDUM RE: JAPANESE ADMINISTRATION METHODS IN EAST INDIES.

A valuable insight into the methods of administration now being adopted in the Dutch East Indies, Burma, the Philippines, and other parts of Eastern Asia, overrun by the Japanese, is provided in the following article from the German Press, written by their correspondent in Japan, Wilhelm Schulze.

"Deutsche Allgemeine Zeitung", Berlin, September 23, 1943.

JAPANESE ADMINISTRATION IN THE OCCUPIED COUNTRIES

Radio Speech by our Reporter in Eastern Asia: Wilhelm Schulze. TOKIO. September 1942.

Military Courts are at the moment still the highest administrative authorities in all the countries which have been taken as military possessions during the war in Eastern Asia, and even the newly-formed Ministry for Greater Eastern Asia is, according to the wish and will of their ancestors, to alter nothing at present. The Ministry will therefore be concentrating its activity meanwhile on those countries which do not belong to this sphere, on which have been conquered further back in the past. But even in the military-administered countries the management of the administration is in different hands in each case.

All conquered countries of Eastern Asia are for the time being under Military Administration, the heads of which are without exception those Generals who have themselves conquered the country. Several countries, not specially named, are administered by the Navy, but the Navy as well as the Army Administrators have all over taken on civil cooperation from Japan, who relieve them of the gubernatorial activities and the civil duties of the Administration and who themselves brought over officials of the middle and lower grades. In the highest quarters, the organisation of which the Japanese Government keep secret for strategic reasons, 312 so-called Administrators General (Hauptverwalter) are working according to the latest statistics as Governors of Prefectures for the Army and 15 for the Navy. There are at the moment about 3,000 so-called Administrators, i.e. first Assistants for the General Administrators, there are 2,000 technicians, several hundred interpreters, and so many office personnel that the total number of Japanese Civil Servants at the moment in the Southern regions amounts to 20,000. They have all been taken from the Japanese official machine in the home country which received in this way a welcome reduction and rejuvenation.

As already mentioned, the Japanese Government has given no intimation whatsoever as to where the seats and working places are of the Administrators-General (Hauptverwalter) among whom are prominent Japanese personages. Only for the major units of territory, such as Burma and the Philippines, are the identities of the Administrators-General ascertainable.

===== Page 126 =====
Apparently, in the cases of Malaya and the South Sea Islands, the old political borders do not coincide with the new, which is understandable in view of such facts that the similarity between Sumatra and Malaya has always been much greater than that between Sumatra and Java, between Celebes and Borneo, or between Celebes and New Guinea. Before uttering any critical judgment upon the new structure, which is thus in process of development, however, we must wait till the Japanese government deems the time to have come for divulging the details.

Naturally, the problem of building up an Eastern Asian sphere of activity is not to be solved with 20,000 men. But these 20,000 represent no more than the skeleton of the new Administration. One day the flesh and blood will come in the form of Japanese Pioneers recruited from private life, thousands of whom have reported voluntarily, but whose numbers will have to be increased by thousands more before the problem is solved. It has been estimated lately by a Japanese expert on these questions that in order really to exploit the Philippines and Malaya 500,000 Japanese would be necessary. It will be easy for Japan to find these people as soon as the war is ended and the armies are demobilised. Up till then only the foundation can be laid for future development in which the Japanese emigrants, who have already before lived and worked in these countries, must and will naturally represent the first wave of the Japanese penetration.

The work will be made easier for the Japanese, inasmuch as the people of Burma and of the Philippines have been promised at the beginning of the war the independence of their states and can count today on obtaining, apart from their military administrations and the civil helpers, Administration Organs which will be recruited from the local population. VARGAS, the former Chief Secretary of the Government of the Philippines, has taken charge of the local administration there, and in Burma Dr. URA LAUNG, the former Prime Minister, is in charge. Both preside, so to speak, over the local Cabinet, and function beside the military administration the internal administration and internal affairs, the form the embryo of future independent Governments. Both have for their assistance the local administrators of Provinces and Layors. Both have - and that is very important - accomplished the break with the British-American past, also internally and have become champions of their compatriots on the march to a new Eastern Asian future.

Eric Rosenthal.
Censor.
Publications Section.

THE CHIEF CENSOR, CAPE TOWN. (3) Submitted to: B.B.C. Reports
JOHANNESBURG.
6th April 1943.

MALAYA.

JAPANESE RECONSTRUCTION IN MALAYA - An escapee from Malaya states that Singapore has not suffered very much. It seems that the concrete buildings were able to withstand the Japanese bombs, which were only able to penetrate the top storey of the houses. He also states that railway communications throughout Malaya have been restored, apparently largely due to the use of forced labour. During the registration of the local inhabitants, the Japanese conscripted every physically able man; in this way, 70,000 men were obtained for repair work and the building of fortifications in North Malaya. 22.20 CHUNGKING MOSLEMS RISING
Nanking: Reports from the Chungking area say that the Chiang Kai-shek regime is desperately trying to suppress the growing number of Moslem uprisings and insults which are fomented by Chinese Communists. As a temporary measure on 8th July, Ma Men-li and Ma Chung-wu, Moslem leaders in Kansu Province, were made members of the Kansu Provisional Government Council, and Pai Chung-hsi, influential among Moslems, has been sent to Kansu. It is understood that Pai Chung-hsi arrived in Lanchow on 7th July.

DONEI (JUP) IN ENGLISH FOR EUROPE N ZONE 11.7.43

06.00 INDIAN PROVINCIAL GOVERNMENT: NATURE AND TASK: BOSE
Shonan: The establishment of a provisional Government for Free India to mobilise all resources of Indians residing in East Asia by thorough organisation, was reiterated by Subhas Chandra Bose, the newly-elected President of the Indian Independence League, in the first Press Review this morning.

"According to my ideas, the Provisional Government won't be a normal peacetime Government," he stressed, "it will be a fighting organisation to organise Indian people and lead them into battle." Bose declared that once the Indians succeed in effacing all Anglo-U.S. influences from India, this provisional Government would make way for a permanent Government of Free India. "When this is established," he said, "then Indians will have to decide for themselves what form their Government will take."

Answering Pressmen's questions, Bose emphasised that his main object at present was twofold: to bring about maximum help for those who were fighting for freedom at home, and once and for all to deal a crushing blow to the enemy. Bose said he was firmly convinced that if the Indians in East Asia mobilized their entire resources now, they would be able to bring to their countrymen at home sufficient help to expel the Anglo-Saxon Powers from India once and for all.

"In order to inspire our countrymen I have given them a new slogan: 'Total mobilization of all our resources'. Half-hearted measures won't do ... All Indians in East Asia who are really anxious for their country's freedom must now come forward in this critical hour and sacrifice all for a speedy emancipation of the Motherland." Bose described this help which loyal Indians outside India would send to their countrymen at home as "a real Second Front".

Outlining plans to mobilise the total resources of the entire Indian population in East Asia, Bose declared that approximately 300,000 soldiers would be raised in East Asia.

Asked his plans for instilling into this army high discipline, he stressed that in addition to military training, intensive moral training would also be given so as to turn them into a highly efficient force. He added: "As for the Indian National Army's efficiency I am confident it will be at least five times greater than that of the enemy."

Those unable through physical or other considerations to swell the ranks of the National Army should give moral and financial support to the best of their ability.

Regarding means whereby he hoped to achieve India's independence, Bose declared that the Indian National Army would play a leading part in the coming struggle. "This army will be further expanded shortly, and it is my intention to form a unit of the Indian army within this army," he said.

Questioned regarding the inclusion of women in the National Army, Bose reminded the interviewer of the Rani of Jhansi, staunch woman patriot of 1857, who rode into battle with her army, adding that the presence of women freedom fighters in the army would serve to heighten national feelings in India.

Asked his attitude towards Gandhi's policy of non-violence, Bose declared all Indians would of course fully appreciate the Mahatma's civil disobedience tactics, but times had changed. Therefore, other means, armed force, had to be sought, in order to lend weight to civil disobedience.

When asked, "Which type of government would the provisional Government adopt; would it be in any way a Democratic Government, for example," the Indian leader counter-questioned in his inimitable manner: "I would like to ask whether there is in any Democracy any Government which can truthfully say it is Democratic in the world today."

===== Page 129 =====
Regarding the Indian people's attitude to Nippon, Bose said that the outbreak of the Greater East Asia war made them realise that Nippon was fighting the common enemy, and moreover that Nippon was able to inflict defeat after defeat on the Anglo-U.S. forces, thus helping India's struggle for freedom. Tojo's assurance that Burma and the Philippines would become independent before the end of the current year would have very favourable repercussions and make Indians appreciate Nippon's sincere intentions.

DOMEI (JUP) IN ENGLISH FOR EUROPEAN ZONE 11.7.43

10.03 GREATER EAST ASIA: NO INFLATION NEPAR: TAKASE
Fukuoka: "There is no fear of inflation in the Southern Regions," Takase declared on his return from a tour of the Southern Regions. Self-sufficiency and increasing the production of war materials constitute what he considers two immediate economic problems. Another problem of a more permanent nature was the establishment of the Greater East Asia economic sphere, based on an interchange of specialised products; for example, tin of Malaysia, rice of Java, or lumber from Thailand among member nations of the Co-prosperity Sphere. Elementary education will be advanced throughout the Southern Regions. Already a greater number of pupils attend primary schools in the south than in pre-war days, but there is great need of Nippongo teachers there.

10.11 INDIAN CURRENCY INFLATION
By line from Domei's Economic commentator Tokio 11.7.
Inflation has gripped India, as the Indian Government is printing large amounts of paper currency in order to meet war expenditure. Rapid increase in the circulation of currency in recent years in India is seen in the following list (units rupees 1,000,000): March, 1939 - 1,880; December, 1939 - 2,250; April, 1942 - 3,950; September, 1942 - 4,390; May, 1943 - 6,250. With the increase in paper currency, there was a jump in commodity prices. This abnormal rise is accelerated by a shortage of commodities caused by a decrease of imports due to lack of shipping, British requisitioning of commodities and the transfer of peace industries to war production. Whereas Indian imports decreased for last year, exports, particularly to England, did not show a noticeable falling off. Commodities most affected by the sudden rise in prices were foodstuffs and manufactured goods. Cost of living among the working classes is said to have risen 60 percent during the past three years. Because of the shortage and high price of foodstuffs, the number of deaths from starvation is said to be increasing even in Bengal, which is a rice-producing State. Another effect of inflation is the tendency to hoard foodstuffs as well as coins, coin-hoarding showing Indian distrust of paper money. A glance at the 1943-44 Budget estimate of the Indian Government reveals that Britain is levying heavier taxes upon the Indian people. Increased taxation may absorb surplus purchasing power, but Britain is collecting taxes without giving anything in return for the maintenance of a minimum standard of living. The Indian Government plans to increase the supply of foodstuffs to India through importation from Australia or by increased production in India itself. But these measures are not effective. Meanwhile, the British authorities are requisitioning foodstuffs and other commodities to feed the Anglo-U.S. forces in West Asia, Africa, and garrisons stationed in India. Guns and ammunition are pouring into India while flowing out are foodstuffs and other daily necessities.

DOMEI (JUP) IN ENGLISH FOR EUROPEAN ZONE 11.7.43

14.35 SULAWESI: RUBBER PAVING MATERIAL DISCOVERED
Medan: The dream of a rubber highway running throughout Greater East Asia Co-prosperity Sphere is destined to become a reality soon with the discovery of a new paving material made of rubber which is claimed equal, if not superior to, asphalt. The new material is a discovery of the East Coast Agriculture Experimental Station of Sumatra. Tests have shown that the new paving material has remarkable wearing and adhesive qualities. 5. SIAM: TOJO'S PROMISE OF NEW TERRITORIES
Bangkok: Tojo's arrival in Bangkok on 3rd July and his formal conference on 4th July with Marshal Pibul Songgran was announced today, Monday. The two Prime Ministers conferred on the whole of the Japanese-Thai relations and exchanged unreserved views on various policies for bringing the current war to a successful conclusion. Complete agreement was reached concerning the problem of incorporating new territories into Thailand and Thailand's future cooperation with Japan. Tojo gave his word to the Thai Prime Minister that the four states in North Malaya: Perlis, Kedah, Kelantan, and Trengganu, and two states in the Shan States: Chieng Tung and Mong-Fan, will be incorporated into the Thai territory. In this connection a joint Japanese-Thai communique was issued at two o'clock Monday afternoon, Bangkok Time.

Tojo's Tour of Southern Regions

10.08 Shonan: The Japanese Premier Gen. Tojo arrived at Shonan at 14:34 in the course of an extensive inspection tour of the southern regions. The Japanese military authorities announced that the purpose of Tojo's visit was "to prepare a new policy in the Southern regions" and to confer with F.M. Hisaichi Terauchi, the Supreme Commander of the Japanese Expeditionary Forces in the Southern Regions, and also to visit officers and men at the front.

17.28 SINGAPORE'S WELCOME TO TOJO
Shonan: Under a veritable sea of Rising Sun flags displayed on every building, the population waved a greeting to Tojo this afternoon. Count Torauchi, Supreme Commander of the Japanese Forces in the Southern Areas, and other prominent Army and Navy officials welcomed him. On arriving at the Central Square he saluted the tremendous crowd which was composed of Japanese, Chinese, Malays, Indonesians, and Indians. Tojo later visited the H.Q. of the Japanese Forces in the Southern Areas where he heard reports from various unit commanders of the Japanese forces.

10.15 TOJO RECEIVES MALAYAN SULTANS
Shonan: Premier Tojo expressed due acknowledgment and profound appreciation for invaluable services rendered by the Sultans and people of Malai from the outset of the current war, at a meeting with nine Sultans of Malai this afternoon. The meeting was attended by the Sultans of Johore, Perak, Selangor, Kedah, Negri Sembilan, Pahang, Kelantan, Trengganu, and Perlis in traditional silken costumes, also by the Supreme Commander of the Southern Japanese Army and other high military officials. Welcoming Tojo, the Sultan of Johore, representing his group said: "Today our hearts are filled by the supreme honour of welcoming your Excellency to Shonan - erstwhile British stronghold for invasion of Asia. We Asiatic races are profoundly moved by the brilliant accomplishments of Japan in the reconstruction of Asia by completely driving out Anglo-Dutch-American influences from this part of the globe." Concluding he said: "On this memorable occasion today paying our respects to your Excellency has made an indelible impression on us, and has served to renew our resolve to collaborate with Japan for the attainment of the common goals of war."

Replying, Tojo thanked the Sultans for their cooperation with the Japanese Military Administration and commended them for their sympathy and realistic appraisal [POSSIBLY MISSING OR UNCLEAR] of events since the beginning of hostilities. He reminded the Sultans that victory in the Pacific War has the condition for the realization of the common ideal of liberated Asia, upon principles of justice. Sultan Ibrahim of Johore said that he was moved by the cordiality with which Tojo had received him and added that Tojo impressed him as a man of action. Sultan Abdul Aziz of Perak said he was grateful for the opportunity of meeting Japan's great leader. It strengthened his resolve for all-out cooperation to Japan. Musahaddih, Sultan of Selangor, said that though he had met a dozen former British Governors, none had received him with such unfeigned geniality as Tojo.

DOMEI (JUP) IN ENGLISH FOR PACIFIC ZONE 10.05; AND IN ENGLISH FOR EUROPEAN ZONE 14.35 4.7.43

(Note: The following speech by S.C. Bose was transmitted in two sections, the first part being transmitted for the Pacific Zone at 10.05, the second part being sent out as a continuation at 14.35 for the European Zone).

S.C. Bose, Indian Independence League's New President, Proclaims Provisional Indian Government

10.05 Shonan: An inspiring address calling for unflinching determination to prepare the Indian people at home and abroad to fight for Indian Independence was delivered by Subhas Chandra Bose on his appointment as President of the East Asia Indian Independence League. He said: Rash Behari Bose and representatives of the Indian Independence Movement in East Asia, I thank you for appointing me leader of the Indian Independence Movement in East Asia. I accept the responsibility with a feeling of extreme humility, and I pray God may grant me strength to do my duty to the satisfaction of my countrymen at home and abroad. If you were to hear my experiences - home and abroad - since the outbreak of the present war you'd feel ... been protecting us from harm, guiding our efforts along the path to victory. This increased my optimism and self-confidence a hundredfold. The time has now come for freedom-loving Indians to act. Action demands military discipline as well as unflinching loyalty to the cause. I, therefore, call upon all my countrymen in East Asia to line up in one solid line under one leadership to prepare for the grim fight ahead of us. I am confident that they will do so. I am glad to tell you of a momentous step taken today which serves to unite in common bonds not only patriotic Indians in East Asia, but all over the world. To my knowledge, this is the first time in recent history that Indians abroad have been united in one organisation to attain a common goal. I have publicly declared several times since I left the homeland in 1941 on an important mission that it was in accordance with the will of the vast majority of my countrymen. Since then, despite all restrictions imposed by the British Secret Service, I have remained in constant touch with my countrymen at home. Today, I can inform you that in the last 12 months, a large number of our representatives have been sent to India from outside from all directions. For those who were captured and shot to death, we shall exact full revenge. But many more were able to evade arrest and, according to latest reports, they are working satisfactorily. Thus patriotic Indians from abroad have been working as genuine trustees of freedom fighters at home. Some of my friends at home hoped at one time that under pressure of the International crisis the British Government would, in its own interest, accede to India's demand for independence. They must have been disillusioned by now - because it is clear that both during and after the war the British Government intends to exploit India more ruthlessly than ever. That is why Field Marshal Lord Wavell is being sent as Viceroy. For me, his appointment is a prophetic event - the writing on the wall. This ever retreating C.-in-C. is destined to be the last Viceroy of India. Moreover, the military, political and economic exploitation of India, which he is bound to intensify, will further embitter the Indian masses and strengthen the gathering forces of revolution. But though India is in for a period of military dictatorship under a new Viceroy, I anticipate that in the future another attempt at compromise with India will be made. This will be nothing more than a bluff or hoax, and our countrymen at home should be prepared in advance to see through it as they did when Sir Stafford Cripps offered empty promises to India in April, 1942. Winston Churchill, supreme representative of the British people, recently said he didn't like even the expression "British Commonwealth", preferring "British Empire". The last Imperialist Prime Minister of England will undoubtedly do his very best to preserve the Empire and any offer he may make to the Indian people will be only for the purpose of deceiving them. But there is no sense in even thinking of compromise with an Empire that will soon disappear. Those of you who have studied the history of freedom movements in other lands must have observed that to achieve Independence two conditions are essential. First, a favourable International situation, and second, the necessary sacrifice and effort. The first condition has been fulfilled. If India had to fight the British Empire singlehanded, our task would have been exceedingly difficult. The Tripartite Powers, however, are fighting our enemy, inflicting staggering defeats, and have lightened our burden. And we have a further advantage. The Tripartite Powers are determined to carry on the war until Anglo-U.S. Imperialism is overthrown. The British Empire, despite its power and might, has been trying to obtain help from every possible quarter.

===== Page 132 =====
The complete lack of activity on the part of the Japanese Air Force against unoccupied China during the past week is very unusual and is probably a record for the year. "I do not recall a similar period since the beginning of hostilities," Chennault declared, adding that this lack of activity is surprising as the Japanese had good weather on many days over their usual target areas. However, the current unfavorable weather in Burma might be forcing the enemy to remove their aircraft from that area, and that would require some delay for reorganization. "And perhaps the Japanese do not want to lose any more aircraft," Chennault added.

16.25 14TH U.S. AIR FORCE ANNIVERSARY

A U.S. air base in S. China: The 14th U.S. Air Force H.Q. on 3rd July celebrated its first birthday after having established the brilliant record of destroying 343 Japanese aircraft confirmed during the year's operations, against overwhelming odds which on one occasion amounted to 31 enemy aircraft against one American. In the same period, U.S. bombers have attacked 35 important Japanese bases ranging in a great arc from Hankow down through Central and South China, Indo-China, and Burma, blasting shipyards, docks, warehouses, coal yards, railway installations, fuel dumps, airfields, river shipping, troop transports and barracks.

Officially taking over from the U.S. Volunteer Group on 4th July last year, the 14th U.S. Air Force has faced a task equalling that of the remarkable "Flying Tigers," and in many respects has done better. Outnumbered in almost every encounter with the Japanese, operating with restricted supplies part of the time, and using what Claire Chennault described as "aircraft which would be considered outmoded in other theatres," the U.S. Air Force has nevertheless inflicted irreparable damage on the Japanese through 152 bombing raids and 2,869 fighter missions during its initial year in China.

During the last two months, the 14th Air Force has advanced into a new phase of its development, coordinating its activity with Chinese ground operations in Western Hupeh along the Yangtse and Tungting lake. Hitting Japanese bases at Ichang, Yochow and Nanchang, and bombing Japanese ground forces at Owchihkow, Hwajung and Shihshou, while fighters have sunk river steamers, blown up locomotives, dive-bombed railway installations and strafed motor supply and troops along the entire Japanese front and rear lines, the 14th have given the Chinese ground forces air support for the first time in China's six-year war against Japan.

The U.S. Air Force has experimented with two projects for cooperating with the Chinese Air Force successfully. The first plan, of attaching Chinese Air Force pilots to U.S. units flying in combat missions, was Chennault's own idea and is still being carried out. The second project involved combined Chinese-U.S. Air Force operations, beginning with the bombing of Ichang on 31st May.

During the first year of operations, the 14th has lost 32 aircraft in action, making an average of nearly 11 Japanese aircraft to one American. And while the Japanese losses nearly always include the crews, the U.S. personnel losses are much lower in ratio, as shown by the fact that only nine pilots were killed and three were missing from the 32 during the year.

The 14th's record has been achieved despite outmoded equipment, lack of supplies and the superior enemy numbers, but in "the due course of time," says Chennault, "when we can meet the Japanese in equal numbers, comparative results should be even more greatly in our favor."

===== Page 133 =====
I warn you, though we are absolutely sure of our final victory, we can never afford to under-estimate the enemy; we should even be prepared for temporary setbacks. We have a grim fight ahead of us, for the enemy is at once powerful, unscrupulous and ruthless. In this final march to freedom, you will have to face hunger, thirst, privation, forced marches and death. Only when you pass this test will freedom be yours. I am content you will do so and thereby bring freedom and prosperity to our enslaved and impoverished land.

DOMEI (JUP) IN ENGLISH FOR EUROPEAN ZONE 3.7.43

22.20 U.S. INDEPENDENCE DAY: MORE FROM KURUSU (Addition to Kurusu's interview on U.S. Independence Day see Domei 17.04 3.7.43) Turning to India he said "It is an act of glaring inconsistency, in the light of U.S. traditions, that the U.S.A. of all nations of the world should oppose the Indian people's desire for freedom. This is an instance of plain self denial by the U.S.A. There is, however, reason to believe that the majority of U.S. people sympathise at heart with this move for liberty in East Asia." He added that notwithstanding propaganda to the contrary, U.S. responsibility for provoking the Pacific conflict was clear. "Let records speak. The U.S.A., by applying political and economic pressure, forced us to fight in defence of our national existence. The U.S. people, subsequently, became involved in actual hostilities through the rash commitments of their misguided and irresponsible leaders!" Condemning Washington's policy towards the Latin Americans Kurusu said: "About 150 years ago, the U.S.A. laid the foundations for a new order in the western hemisphere. But, mainly through her rise in wealth and power her foreign policy assumed an increasingly meddlesome tone, in matters that did not concern her. When the war in East Asia ends and pan-American neighbourly policy returns, the Latin American republics will, I trust, be among the first countries to recognise the justice of our new East Asia policy."

22.38 MONGOLIA WILL HELP JAPAN: PRESIDENT Kalgan: Prince Teh, on the sixth anniversary of the outbreak of the war with China reiterated Mengchiang's determination to push forward, hand in hand with Japan, for the satisfactory consummation of the war in Greater East Asia. He declared that the war in Greater East Asia had reached a decisive stage. Since the Anglo-Americans had exploited various peoples of Greater East Asia, all East Asiatics were required to redouble their efforts to crush the common enemy. The Mongolian people, with constant assistance from Japan, had exerted their utmost efforts for the establishment of a Greater East Asia co-prosperity sphere. Mongolia would redouble her efforts to increase production.

06.09 N. CHINA: CHU SHEN DEAD Peking: Chu Shen, Chairman of the North China Political Affairs Commission, died here on 26th June at the age of 65. Chu Shen was appointed Chairman of the Commission in February 1943. The Information Bureau of the North China Political Affairs Commission announced today: "Chu Shen, Chairman of the North China Political Affairs Commission, who has been suffering from Jaundice, died at 03.00 on 26th June." After reporting his death to the National Government the Commission held an extraordinary meeting on 2nd July and decided to appoint Wang Shiching as Acting Chairman pending the appointment of Chu Shen's successor by the National Government. The National Government in the meantime decided to appoint Wang Kehmin as supreme advisor of the North China Political Affairs Commission as new Chairman. His investiture is scheduled to be held on 5th July.

06.15 TOJO'S SMITH: NANKING FINANCE MINISTER Nanking: Chou Fohai, Finance Minister and Vice-President of the Executive Yuan, in a statement to Domei today, expressed his profound gratitude for Premier Tojo's Diet declaration regarding the proposed revision of the existing Chinese-Japan Treaties and predicted that with Chinese cooperation Japanese victory in the Greater East Asia War is certain. With Japan's fighting strength greatly augmented through the development of the southern regions, he added, it will be the Anglo-U.S. that will suffer from a protracted war. Ever since the National Government of China's declaration of war on Britain and the U.S.A., Chinese-Japanese relations had been further cemented, Chou said, recalling that in response to President Wang Ching-Wei's declaration of sharing a common fate with Japan, Japan stated she is ready to retrocede the extraterritorial rights as well as the concessions in China. Japan has not only fulfilled the aforementioned promise but transferred to the National Government enemy assets in China, economic control of business concerns.

===== Page 134 =====
It is, therefore, but natural that we too should look for sympathy and assistance wherever it is available. Moreover, every freedom movement in history had to seek some help or other from abroad before it could achieve success. The logic of events in the present case made the Tripartite Powers our natural allies. There is nothing wrong if we accept their sympathy or even help should we need it. The Tripartite Powers in the past often clarified their attitude to India. In addition, the Japanese Government, through its worthy Prime Minister, Gen. Tojo, has repeatedly proclaimed its policy to the Philippines, Burma and India. British politicians and propagandists, being hypocrites, have described Japan's attitude as insincere and hypocritical. But Prime Minister Tojo dealt a crushing blow to Anglo-U.S. propaganda by boldly declaring that independence will be a reality for Burma and the Philippines - not after the war but before the end of the year. Japan's attitude to Burma and the Philippines is convincing proof of her sincerity and good faith. But apart from this, as a normal human being I see no reason why I should have any doubt or mistrust of Japan's intentions. Japan was the first Asiatic power successfully to resist foreign aggression, and Japan knows, more than any other Asiatic Power, that as long as enslaved Asiatic nations are not emancipated, no Asiatic nations can feel completely safe from aggression. Moreover, there is in Japan today what one might call an "Asiatic consciousness" which manifests itself in a desire to help other Asiatic nations to achieve their liberation. This is a unique development which affords a golden opportunity to all enslaved nations in Asia to emancipate themselves and set up a New Order based on freedom, justice and morality.

14.35 As I said in Tokio the other day, if the British Government could not demoralise me after persecuting me all my life, nobody else can do so. And if cunning British politicians could neither cajole nor deceive me, no one else can hope to do so. Every Indian should realise that victory for the Anglo-U.S. Powers will mean for India continued enslavement and more ruthless exploitation. Our only hope of freedom, therefore, is in a Tripartite victory. But we should so conduct our own struggle that the Axis victory will simultaneously bring us our liberty. Friends! We have now the most favourable international situation, a most happy combination of circumstances. Consequently, all that is needed for winning freedom is sufficient effort and sacrifices. Our record, in this connection, is by no means unsatisfactory. You may remember in May last year, after the departure of Sir Stafford Cripps from India, and exactly 85 years after the outbreak of our first war of Independence, I declared our national struggle was entering upon the most significant phase. Since then we have passed many milestones on our march, the most important being the intensification of the civil disobedience movement, and the start of sabotage activities after the arrest of Mahatma Gandhi last August. India's struggle in August 1942 will, therefore, remain an unforgettable landmark in history, indicating transition from passive to active resistance. Not content with the civil disobedience campaign the Indian people are now morally prepared to employ other means to achieve liberation. The time has, therefore, come to pass on to the next stage of our campaign. All organisations, whether inside or outside India, must now transform themselves into a disciplined fighting organisation under one leadership. The aim and purpose of this organisation should be to take up arms against British Imperialism when the time is ripe and the signal given.

Provisional Government to Prepare for Armed Struggle

To mobilize all our forces effectively, I intend to organise a provisional Government of Free India. It will be the task of this provisional Government to lead the Indian revolution to a successful conclusion. To this end the provisional Government will prepare the Indian people - inside and outside India - for an armed struggle which will be the culmination of all our national efforts since 1895. When the revolution succeeds and Anglo-U.S. Imperialism is expelled from India, the task of the provisional Government will be over. It will then make room for a permanent Government to be set up inside India in accordance with the will of the Indian people. When all our preparations for the last struggle are complete, it will be possible to bring the Indian struggle into line with the common struggle of the Tripartite Powers against the common foes. By participating in this common fight we shall be qualifying for our freedom. By shedding our blood in the sacred cause, we shall be paying the price for liberty and, at the same time, we shall be laying an enduring foundation for our national unity. And last, but not least, by winning freedom through our own efforts and sacrifices, we shall be acquiring strength whereby we shall preserve our liberty for all time.

09.32 R.B. BOSE'S Tribute to S.C. BOSE
Shonan: "This is one of the proudest moments of my life because I have by my side a compatriot who symbolizes all that is best in the Youth of India," declared Rash Behari Bose, President of the Indian Independence League in East Asia in an interview with Domei. He added: "Subhas Bose represents the hope and glory of India. He is virile, daring, dauntless. I have welcomed Subhas with open arms. As long as breath is in my body I shall not spare myself in giving all I can, wholehearted cooperation, assistance and advice, in the fight for India's freedom." Subhas now will march on confident of victory—the victory of India. And what more can I wish than India's victory? I say once again that this is one of the proudest and happiest moments of my life."

Meanwhile, news of Subhas Chandra Bose's arrival in Shonan to lead the Indian Independence Movement swept like an ocean breeze across the peninsula. Feeling among the Indians is that victory is now assured and the time has come for every Indian to show his willingness to make any sacrifice their great leader may demand of them. Typical of many comments heard in the city was: "Indians in East Asia wholeheartedly welcome Subhas Bose's arrival here to lead the final campaign for freeing India," declared the leader of the Shonan Moslem community, Kasanwari. He added that the arrival of so broad-minded and well-known an Indian leader as Subhas Bose was indeed a happy augury for the future independence of India.

Jathivy, Chairman of the Indian Independence League Malai Branch, said that Subhas Bose's arrival here was an epoch-making event in the history of the Indian struggle for freedom; his leadership brought Indian freedom within sight. He paid a glowing tribute to the work of Rash Behari Bose in nurturing the delicate plant of the Independence Movement in East Asia through difficult days and bringing it up to its healthy state.

15.34 R.B. BOSE's Calling to Indian Independence League
Shonan: The text of Rash Behari Bose's address before delegations of Indian Independence League branches in East Asia:

"Friends and Comrades in Arms: It is indeed a great pleasure for myself, and for you all, that we meet today so soon after our last conference in Shonan. But events are marching fast these days, and our movement for the sacred cause of Mother India has made enormous strides during the two months since our last conference. Today we are on the eve of the most vital, and decisive phase of our fight for freedom. I am confident we are on the threshold of victory.

Friends! It is now one and a half years since the Indian independence movement originated in East Asia. For all practical purposes, the historic day, 8th December 1941, when Japan unsheathed the sword in righteousness to destroy Anglo-U.S. Imperialism, and liberate the Asiatic nations from their bondage, marked the inception of the Indian independence movement in its present form. You know we started from scratch, with nothing but the indomitable spirit of service to our Motherland. But soon we found sincere friends and powerful Allies, and the movement gathered strength, thanks to your efforts and cooperation and thanks to the patriotic fervour of Indians throughout East Asia. And our most sincere gratitude is due to our Japanese friends, so the Government of Japan, to local military authorities, and every part of East Asia and the Japanese nation in general.

Friends, and comrades! As you all know very well, we have had our share of trials and tribulations. But, thanks to your grim resolve, our movement survived all the obstacles in its way, and emerged with increased strength and solidarity."

BOSE: SINGAPORE INDIAN INDEPENDENCE LEAGUE

Shonan: Commenting on Subhas Chandra Bose's arrival here, the spokesman of the Indian Independence League H.Q. stated: "Subhas Chandra Bose arrived in Shonan to take an active part in the Indian independence movement in East Asia and to plunge into battle for India's liberation. To the Indians of Shonan, the arrival of Subhas Bose in their midst is a source of great inspiration. To the Indian independence movement in East Asia, the very presence of Subhas Bose is a source of immense strength, and to millions of Indian nationalists at home waging a heroic battle against Britain, the efforts of Subhas Bose in East Asia are a source of great encouragement and confidence in victory. This day marks a new epoch in the Indian fight against British Imperialism, and also marks a new epoch in the Holy War for the liberation of Asia from Anglo-U.S. tyranny and exploitation."

Pointing out that Subhas Bose was an Indian leader of worldwide renown, ranking among such illustrious sons of India as Gandhi, Maulana Azad, Pandit, the spokesman declared: "Throughout his life he has been in the thick of the fight against India's enemy. He is the most uncompromising opponent of British rule in India; and he dedicated his life to the sacred cause of freedom for India. Bose's views on India's fight for freedom are simple, straightforward and highly practical. He was convinced there can be no compromise whatever between Indian nationalism and British Imperialism. He advocates direct decisive action: 'When the blood of freedom-loving Indians begins to flow, India will attain her freedom.' To India's freedom fighters Subhas Bose sent this message of victory: 'India shall be free - and before long.' And he has given this assurance to the Indian nation: 'When the right moment arrives I, and many others like myself, will be by your side to share the glory, fighting and suffering side-by-side and sharing the joy of victory as well.' That is Subhas Bose's mission - a mission in which he is confident of victory and in which he will have the wholehearted support of 2,000,000 Indians in East Asia."

Referring to the keen interest with which Indians in Shonan have been awaiting his arrival and the enthusiastic response by Indians in East Asia to his appeals broadcast from Tokio, the spokesman said: "It offers conclusive evidence of the grim resolve of the Indian people to sacrifice their all in the fight into which Subhas Bose will soon plunge himself body and soul. India, following the arrival of Subhas Bose in East Asia, offers striking indication of the certainty of India's victory in the battle for independence. For nearly one and a half years the Indian Independence League in East Asia, under the leadership of Behari Bose, has been mobilizing Indian manpower and material resources to launch a final battle to crush the Anglo-U.S. forces of aggression in India. And, in this great task, the Indian Independence Movement has had invaluable assistance and the wholehearted cooperation of the Japanese Government and local authorities in East Asia, besides the sympathy and support of other Asiatic nations and the entire right-thinking world."

Declaring the arrival of Subhas Bose had given fresh impetus to the Indian Independence Movement, the spokesman concluded: "With the unstinting guidance, support, and cooperation of Rash Behari Bose, and with the unswerving loyalty and assistance of 2,000,000 Indians in East Asia, Subhas Chandra Bose will, in his own words, 'organise such a gigantic force that it will sweep away British power from India.'"

9. BOSE: CANTON INDIANS MEET

Chandra Bose's visit to Japan has given a great impetus to the Indian move for independence. A general meeting of the local branch of the Indian Independence League was held in Canton on 2nd July. One hundred Indian residents attended and were asked to give their full support to the head office of the movement in Singapore, where they were going shortly.

===== Page 138 =====
GTP AND CB: ATTENTION MR. KEATING, COLONIAL OFFICE ALSO.

60.

DOMEI IN ENGLISH FOR AMERICAN ZONE. 17.28. 5.7.43.

SINGAPORE'S DELIRIOUS WELCOME TO TOJO.

SHONAN: BURIED UNDER A VERITABLE SEA OF SUN FLAGS AS ALL BUILDINGS IN THE CITY WERE DECORATED WITH JAPAN'S NATIONAL COLOURS AND THE POPULACE WILDLY WAVED FLAGS TO GREET JAPAN'S WARTIME PREMIER WHO ARRIVED THIS AFTERNOON. TOJO WAS GREETED BY FIELD MARSHAL COUNT TERAUCHI, SUPREME COMMANDER OF THE JAPANESE FORCES IN THE SOUTHERN AREAS AND ALSO BY OTHER VERY PROMINENT MEN OF THE ARMY AND NAVY AS WELL AS CIVILIANS AND OTHER NOTABLES. TOJO DROVE THROUGH THE STREETS OF SHONAN DENSELY LINED ON BOTH SIDES BY CHEERING CROWS. ARRIVING AT THE CENTRAL SQUARE, TOJO MOUNTED A SPECIAL STAND, SALUTED THE TREMENDOUS GATHERING WHICH GAVE A DEAFENING OVATION TO THE JAPANESE PREMIER. THE CROWD WHICH ASSEMBLED AT THE CENTRAL SQUARE WAS COMPOSED OF JAPANESE, CHINESE, MALAIS, INDONESIANS, AND INDIANS.

(CONTINUATION OF SERIAL 60. P. 2).

DOMEI INTERVIEWS LOCAL INHABITANTS.

THE DOMEI CORRESPONDENT ASKING A MALAI STUDENT OF THE ASIA DEVELOPMENT TRAINING INSTITUTE WHAT HE THOUGHT OF TOJO'S VISIT SAID: "IT HAS FILLED US WITH OVERWHELMING EMOTION AND GRATITUDE. REGARDLESS OF RACE AND CREED TODAY A FEELING OF STRONGER DUTY TO EXERT OURSELVES TO THE UTMOST TO WIN FINAL VICTORY."

AN INTERVIEWED INDIAN MERCHANT SAID: "SINCERITY BEHIND THE ALL OUT AID PROMISED BY TOJO TO INDIA FOR INDEPENDENCE HAS BEEN CONFIRMED BY THE PREMIER'S PRESENT VISIT TO SHONAN."

NO BRITISH PREMIER VISITED SINGAPORE.

A CHINESE TELEPHONE OPERATOR SAID: "NOT ONCE DID A PREMIER VISIT SHONAN WHEN IT WAS UNDER BRITISH RULE. THAT IS WHY WE ARE OVERJOYED BY TOJO'S VISIT AND WILL NOT, FOR THE REST OF OUR LIVES, FORGET THIS HISTORIC EVENT."

THE PREMIER LATER PROCEEDED TO THE HEADQUARTERS OF THE JAPANESE FORCES IN THE SOUTHERN AREAS WHERE HE HEARD REPORTS OF THE VARIOUS UNIT COMMANDERS OF THE JAPANESE FORCES.

NATIVE PRINCES.

TOJO AND TERAUCHI RECEIVED NATIVE PRINCES OF THE OCCUPIED AREAS WHO CAME TO PAY THEIR RESPECTS TO THE JAPANESE PREMIER.

(D.B.C. MONITORING). ++19.45. 5.7. 0. (F.M.)

With the Compliments of the Under Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs

May 5th, 1943.

I have the honour to forward a report written by a Chinese named Dan Pak Choon (覃拔崖) on conditions in Malaya from the date of the Japanese occupation until his escape to Free China via Thailand on 26th December, 1942. Mr. Dan, who is twenty-three years old, claims to have been born at Alor Star, Kedah.

2. An additional copy is attached for transmission to the Colonial Office.

With the highest respect,

===== Page 140 =====
My Brief Biography

1916: I was born in Alor Star, capital of the State of Kedah, Malaya. My father was then running a provision shop (grocery). I had a brother who was six years older than I.

1917: My dear mother died.

1922: When I was seven years old, I was sent to a primary school while my father had made much profit and he, in addition to his shop, ran a biscuit factory. My brother returned to China.

1926: 11 years old. I began to learn in a senior primary school. My father became a rubber estate owner. I had my stepmother.

1927: 12 years old. My father and I went to Hainan Island, our native land. I entered a middle school. My father came back to Malaya the same year. I lived with my uncle and my brother.

1928: My brother went to Canton and received his education in a missionary school.

1932: 17 years old. I was a graduate of the Senior Middle School.

1933: Returned to Malaya again. I studied English in Anglo-Chinese School in Kedah. I started learning in the third-year class. My father engaged a Malay to teach me Malay language at home at night. During this period of time, I associated with many members of the Malay Royal Families.

1938: 22 years old. I went to Penang and passed my Junior Cambridge Examination in the Saint Xavier's School.

1939: 23 years old. I took my father's place as Manager of our shop, biscuit factory, and rubber estate. Simultaneously, I was elected as General Secretary of the Kedah Chinese China Distress Relief Fund Committee. I devoted myself to the task of raising money for the war refugees in China. On behalf of the Committee, I often called on the High Government Officers to discuss methods of how to raise money. I was always encouraged by them. I was also a correspondent to many Chinese newspapers, sending them news and occasionally writing some comments.

===== Page 141 =====
1940
Through the kind invitation of the Chinese Government, the South-Seas Overseas Chinese organised a Comfort Mission to go to China. I was elected as representative to join the Mission. We made a journey of about 40,000 li and went through 11 provinces. In Chungking we saluted the President Lin Sen and Marshal Chiang Kai-shek. Returned to Malaya via Hong Kong in the month of September. Mrs. Shenton Thomas (Sir Shenton Thomas was the Governor in Singapore) sponsored the establishment of the Patriotic Fund in Malaya to raise funds for the relief of war orphans and refugees in England. A branch committee was formed in Kedah. I was a committee member of it. Many times we held charity shows to collect money for the fund.

1941
Through my friends' recommendation, I became a sub-contractor. I erected temporary sheds and constructed airplane landing grounds for the R.A.F. and the Public Works Department of the Kedah Government. In April, I made an appeal to the Members of the Chinese School Union (I was then the President) to join the Medical Auxiliary Service. I was appointed by the British Adviser and Dr. Beathee, our officers in charge, as superintendent of the said service. On the very day of December 8th, when Japan declared war on Great Britain and the United States of America, we were called for mobilisation and we assembled at once getting ready for work. On the 12th, three days before the fall of Alor Star, we were ordered to pull off our uniforms.

1942
The Japanese Gendarmes came to Alor Star in February when I was arrested. My offence was "helping the British and Chungking Government." After two weeks imprisonment, I was released but had been forced to be a member of the Chinese Peace Preservation Committee, a puppet organ directed by the Japanese. I spent most of my time doing my own business. I often talked with some members of Malay Royal Families and High Officers. They dared say nothing and were very disappointed but they could not do anything under Japanese high pressure. One day, I learnt that the Japanese troops stationed on the Malayan-Thai Border would leave for Singapore on December 26th. So I

===== Page 142 =====
Prepared to escape. Two days after the Japanese Armies' departure, I immediately left Kedah for Thailand. The policemen at the border were my good friends, so they let me go. I obtained my certificate of Aliens from the Thai Immigration Office at Sadao (shown in the map below) after giving a bribe of 300 Thai dollars to the officers.

In 1943, I stayed in Haadyai for three days. On January 1st, I went to Bangkok by train. I received a travelling passport from the Thai Ministry for Foreign Affairs through my friend's help. Then I went to the French Consulate-General to have my passport endorsed. On the 20th, I left Bangkok by train. The first night I stopped at Kolat, the second night at Ubon, and on the third day we reached a border town named Mukdahan, which was situated by the side of a river forming the natural boundary between Thailand and French Indo-China. The next morning, after being strictly examined by the Thai Customs Officers, I crossed the river and reached Samandakek. The French Authorities examined me more strictly and took away my passport for examination. After getting my passport back, I started for Dongha by truck, and from Dongha I took the train to Haiphong. At Haiphong, all passengers underwent a very strict examination and inquiry by the Japanese and French officers. When the examination was over, we boarded a Japanese ship to Kwongchowwan. I left Kwongchowwan on February 6th and arrived in Chungking on the 28th of the same month.

===== Page 144 =====
How Japanese Managed

The Supervisory of Japanese Military and Political Affairs (軍政監部) in the Southern Regions was the Japanese Emperor's uncle; his duty was to supervise the two below-mentioned headquarters. He had his office in Singapore (now called Syonan-to. "Syonan" meant that the Japanese Emperor's descendants had expanded southwards and "to" meant island).

The Headquarters of the Japanese Southern Regions Expeditionary Army (日岸南方派遣軍司令部) was in Singapore with General Terauchi (寺内寿一大將) as its head.

The Headquarters of Political Affairs Department (軍政本部) was a supreme organ in charge of all political and civil affairs in Malaya with Colonel Tanabe (渡邉大佐) as its head.

In Penang, Malacca, and in every Malay state (Johore, Negri Sembilan, Selangor, Perak, Kedah including Perlis, Kelantan, Trengganu, and Pahang), it had a branch office called Department of State Political Affairs (州政廳).

In the State of Kedah, the organisation of the Department, as far as I know, is as follows:

===== Page 145 =====
(2 Japanese Officers)
Consulting Council (3 members of Malay Royal Families)
(2 other prominent Malays)

Head of Board of Religious Affairs - the Sultan or Regent (宗務院院長)

Secretary to Board of Religious Affairs - (Malay) (宗務院秘書)

Education Section (教育科) (Japanese)

Board of General Affairs (華僑責任者) (Japanese) (總務部) (Japanese) [forgotten]

Accounting Section (會計科) (Japanese)

Board of Finance (財務部) (Japanese) (計算科) (Japanese) [forgotten]

GOVERNOR OF THE STATE (州長官)

Agricultural Affairs Section (農業科) (Malay)

Industrial, Commercial and Fishery Section (工商水産科) (Malay)

Sanitary Affairs Section (醫生科) (Malay)

Land Affairs Section (土地科) (Malay) [forgotten]

Special and Secret Affairs (特高科) (Japanese)

Peace Maintenance Section (保安科) (Malay)

Land and Water Communication (交通科) (Japanese)

Petrol Rationing Section (瓦斯配給科) (Japanese) [forgotten]

Communication (交通部) (Japanese) [forgotten]

===== Page 146 =====
The organization of other states' departments was almost the same.

Names of other Governors of States are as follows:

Penang: Lieut.-General Katayama Shotaro
Kolantan: A Major-General
Malacca: Ex-Consul-General in Singapore
Johore: A Major-General
Perak: A Civil Officer
Selangor: A Civil Officer
Negri Sembilan: A Civil Officer

Military

British War Prisoners and public servants were retained in a concentrated camp on Bukit Changgi Island just opposite Singapore town.

Australian War Prisoners all had become coolies; they worked hard all day. We could see them everywhere in Singapore. No new clothes or sufficient food were supplied to them.

About 10-15 thousand of them had been sent to Thailand to construct a railway line connecting Thailand to Burma. Most of them wore only a pair of short pants.

The Indian War Prisoners were freed. They were reorganized and named "Indian National Army" (印度国家军) and "Indian Independent Working Corps" (印度独立劳动军). They were under Japanese command and training and were badly treated. They were stationed at the following places: Alor Star, Ipoh, Kuala Lumpur, Johore, Singapore, and Kelantan.

Immediately after the fall of North Malaya, on the Malayan-Thai border line, 80 Indian soldiers surrendered themselves to the Japanese Army. On the next day, they were all stabbed to death.

===== Page 147 =====
Productions

Rubber:

A company was established to buy the rubber productions. It was named "The Syonan Rubber Syndicate" (昕南蘺蘇組合), which was invested in by both the Japanese Government and many big firms in Tokyo.

The regulated price for the standard-class rubber was $26.60 per picul. Rubber of bad classes was not accepted.

Its head office was in Singapore, and it had branches (出張所) in every state with Japanese managers who authorised rubber merchants of various races, most of them Chinese, to collect rubber for them.

Tin Ore:

All tin ore might be sold to the Japanese, price being $50 per picul (less than £100 per ton).

Iron Scrap:

Iron scrap had been largely collected and heaped up everywhere.

But Japan had too few ships for transportation, so only a small quantity of the above-mentioned Malayan productions had been shipped to Japan.

From the State of Kedah, the Japanese exported monthly 30,000 to 40,000 bags of rice to unknown places for military use, causing starvation among the inhabitants in the State of Kedah and nearby states.

Eggs, fowls, cows, and many other kinds of foodstuffs were bought in large quantities and sent to unknown places.

They also collected gold and jewels.

===== Page 148 =====
Finance

Immediately after North Malaya was occupied, Japanese note-money began circulating. Up to last December, it was said that there were 300 to 500 million dollars of this money in circulation.

Old currency was being used. The exchange rate was one to one. Black market M.Y.I = ¥c.90.

The Yokohama Specie Bank Ltd. (横渡正金銀行) had its Head Office established in Singapore, with branches spread all over Malaya.

The Taiwan Banking Corporation, Ltd. also opened in Singapore.

The Bank of China and the Bank of Kwangtung Province were sealed.

Banks run by Chinese or Indian merchants without relations to their respective Governments were allowed to continue their business.

Communication

Railway communication was restored in May last year. One could travel through Malaya, from Singapore in the south to Padang Besar in the north. It took 48 hours to complete this journey. Only the third-class compartment was available.

On the train, Japanese gendarmes examined passengers very strictly.

Last September, the Tokyo Trolley-Bus Co. Ltd. (東京急行電車株式会社) began managing road communication throughout Malaya.

Junks were regarded as the only means for traveling to Sumatra.

There was no through communication between Thailand and Malaya for the public.

===== Page 149 =====
Police

The former police system was temporarily maintained.

All policemen were called back to work and out of them, the young and the strong were chosen to be organised in "Special Police Corps" (特別警察隊). They first might swear to be loyal to the so-called "His Majesty the Imperial Emperor" (天皇陛下). They were comparatively well-paid and treated. They had to undergo strict military training. They were ordered to get ready at any moment to go to the front to fight.

More men would be recruited for this kind of "police".

Some "good and loyal" Malay police officers were sent to Singapore to get special training.

The police received order to take a census of all inhabitants in Malaya. It was completed in the month of October last. Again the police received order to register all men whose ages were between 16 to 40.

Education

All English schools were not allowed to open. Most of these schools were used for barracks.

China, Malay and Indian primary schools were re-opened. Japanese language was being taught half of the school-time, and another half their respective language. The school teachers had to learn Japanese for a few hours a day so that they would be able to teach their students. It was learnt that, starting from the year 1944(?), Japanese will be the only curriculum in all schools.

Malay Colleges and Chinese High Schools were not opened.

From July this year, all letters would be written and addressed in Japanese, otherwise they would be undelivered.

"Asiatic Training Institute" (馬里訓練所) was established in Singapore in May last. From every state, 5 to 10 clever youths or Government servants were [POSSIBLY MISSING]

===== Page 150 =====
Sent to learn in this Institute every three months, and those whose results were good would proceed to Tokyo for higher education.

English, Chinese, and Indian newspapers were published in Singapore, Penang, and Kuala Lumpur. Malay papers were published in many main towns.

As from the year 1945, the Japanese paper would be the only paper that we could read; it was so planned by the Japanese.

All papers were under the supervision of the "Japanese Military Propaganda Section" (軍宣傳班).

Enemy Property

British and American properties were regarded as enemy properties. Their firms were confiscated. All debts owed to the firms before the war had to be paid to the Japanese authorities.

British and American Rubber Estates were under the management of the "Syonan Rubber Syndicate." Some rubber estates were re-opened for tapping.

In some places, the rubber trees had been cut down and vegetables were grown instead.

Indian

Every State had an "Indian Independent League" (印度獨立聯盟). Mr. Bose spent many months' time in Malaya last year.

The Chettiar (Indian Usurers) were not allowed to collect interest from their debtors.

Tens of thousands of Indian Rubber Estate Coolies were thrown out of work. Many starved to death.

Thousands of them were employed by the Japanese Air Force to construct air bases and were badly paid.

The Indian Independent League had their own flag.

===== Page 151 =====
Chinese

The people who hated Japanese the most were Chinese, but under Japanese tyrannical oppression, they had to give way.

In Singapore, by Japanese order, an "Overseas Chinese Union" (华侨协会) had been formed and in every state it had a branch. Its duty was to help maintain peace and collect war funds for them.

Last year, this "Union" was ordered to collect 50 million dollars as a "Donation" to the so-called "His Imperial Emperor."

In Singapore, 15,000 strong and young Chinese were arrested and thrown into the deep sea secretly at night. In Penang, 5,000 were prisoners and starved to death. In many other towns, a total number of another 5,000 were mysteriously lost.

The Chinese national flag was ordered not to be hoisted.

Malay

Before the war, because most of the Malay people were cheated by Japanese false propaganda, they liked or rather welcomed the Japanese to come to Malaya to chase out all "White Men" and "Chinamen" and let them have all the properties of the exiled. But now they knew that they were absolutely wrong, for conditions now in Malaya were even worse than before.

The Sultans and Regents had no more actual power. They were only in charge of religious affairs now. The words "His Highness" were prohibited to use. Their salary was reduced. No more royal allowance was given.

The Malay States Flags, like Chinese, were prohibited to be raised; they had to hoist the Japanese flag instead.

The Japanese took all the high positions in the Government Organs, and the Malays had to go to the lower class acting as petty officers.

Despite that the Malays were Mohammedans, the Japanese Army often forced them to try pork and occasionally to have their pigs butchered in the Malay mosques.

===== Page 152 =====
10.25 MALAYA'S RAPID DEVELOPMENT
Domei Correspondent Shonan.
One year and a half of careful and sympathetic direction under the subduing hand of the Japanese military administration has resulted in phenomenal progress throughout the Malay Peninsula.

The vigorous and sincere guidance given by the military administration has not only injected new life into the Malays but has gone a long way towards erasing the corruption which thrived under the long tyranny of the British. Although only a partial picture of the rapid development is obtainable, the survey your correspondent has made of conditions along the western coast of the peninsula suffices to show the tremendous progress achieved.

Any fears which might be entertained as to how the tremendous surplus of rubber can be used are allayed by one look at the rubber-liquefaction plant in Selangor Province. Under British rule, there was not a single liquefaction plant in the entire peninsula. It is expected that the Selangor plant will revolutionize oil production in Greater East Asia when in full-time operation.

With the problem of surplus rubber solved, the authorities are making a tremendous effort to convert Malaya to self-sufficiency in foodstuffs. Hitherto the staple food of Malayans, rice, has been imported from Thailand and French Indo-China, resulting in an undeveloped state of agriculture throughout the peninsula.

A radical change is now taking place. Everybody is now busily engaged in clearing the jungles and opening up idle land for farming. Besides these activities, a number of schools are teaching the inhabitants scientific agriculture. Governor Ken Tsurumi of Malacca State says that more than 6,000 acres have been developed as paddy fields since last year by planting a twice-yearly crop of Taiwan rice.

Cultivators were finding a new enthusiasm in their work, as the schools were now giving four hours of instruction weekly in the latest agricultural techniques.

Malaya, reborn since the British "rubber first" policy, is turning to production of daily necessities, such as paper, textiles, and soap, which were hitherto imported from foreign countries. For example, paper is now being produced from pulp obtained from bamboo reeds and old rubber trees. The supply of materials for pulp is practically unlimited.

Manufacture of soap, which was mainly confined to Shonan, is now spreading to other regions of the peninsula. Soap manufacture in Johore State is making satisfactory progress.

DOMEI (DOA 3) IN ENGLISH FOR PACIFIC ZONE 8.6.43

11.00 MALAYA APPROACHING FOOD SELF-SUFFICIENCY
Domei Correspondent, Shonan

Malaya is now well on the way to self-sufficiency in foodstuffs under the Japanese military administration’s vigorous rehabilitation policy. New vigor has entered every phase of the peninsula’s life.

After the fall of Singapore, Malaya was faced with the problem of disposing of a gigantic rubber surplus. There are hopeful signs that this problem will soon be solved.

Throughout Malaya there are now many experimental plants engaged in turning rubber to other uses. It is estimated that, when rubber liquefaction is firmly established in Malaya, oil production will be revolutionized in the Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere.

Regarding food production, large tracts of jungle land are now being cleared all along the peninsula’s central highway, assuring self-sufficiency in foodstuffs. Formerly Malaya imported staple food such as rice from French Indo-China, with the result that the entire peninsula devoted only a small area to agriculture.

Now, through the efforts of the Japanese authorities, 6,000 additional acres of paddy fields have been developed since last year. Production has been further greatly increased by the importation of rice plants from Taiwan.

Meanwhile, agricultural training schools have been established and are playing an important role in establishing new agricultural methods. Even primary schools are now giving lessons in agriculture, and agricultural institutes have been opened for special advanced courses.

With regard to manufactured goods, Malaya formerly imported paper, cloth, soap and had no industry worth mentioning. Under the new conditions, a number of native factories are now producing these daily necessities from local materials.

===== Page 153 =====
Any further communication on this subject should be addressed to: The Under-Secretary of State, The War Office (as opposite) and the following number quoted.

Tel. No.— WHITEHALL 9400. Ext. 624.

THE WAR OFFICE,
Whitehall,
S.W.1.

162

(Enclo:— GHQ India M.I.S. No. 78 dated 30th April, 1943).
