Confidential

Following information was given to a member of my staff on 16th October by General Wu Te Chen who controls Kuomintang organisation collecting information from occupied territories. Its accuracy cannot be vouched for, though accounts of bad treatment of British prisoners and Chinese population tallies generally with reports previously communicated to my Military Attaché by the same source.

2. The Chinese filtering through from Malay report wholesale shooting of Chinese and that the British prisoners are compelled to do coolie work in great heat under the supervision of Indians drawn from prisoners of war of whom many are alleged to be working for the Japanese. General Wu Te Chen assumes that a careful check is being kept on any alien who may enter India from Burma.

3. The Chinese who left Singapore on 26th July has [POSSIBLY MISSING TEXT].

===== Page 248 =====
Has reported the death of Sir Shenton Thomas. The Japanese are alleged to have compelled him to watch the prisoners at work.

Government of India please pass to War Office, India.

===== Page 249 =====
In amplification of information given regarding certain events at Singapore after its capitulation, J.H. Kortright of the Chartered Bank of India and J. McG. Taylor of the Hongkong and Shanghai Bank make the following statement:

We were at Saigon when a party of Frenchmen were evacuated from Singapore to Saigon in July 1942. Mr. Kortright came in contact with a M. Gaudard, and Mr. Taylor met M. Gaudard and a friend of his whose name he unfortunately cannot remember.

M. Gaudard informed us that he was manager of a French tin mine at Ipoh, that although he was a volunteer, when the invasion took place things were so disorganized that the volunteers in his district did not function, and he, being an ex-Service man, was able to join up with an Indian regiment. This regiment fought back as far as Muar at which place Gaudard was advised to leave for Singapore as a civilian.

This he did, and after the fall of Singapore was left at liberty for some time, living with a Roman Catholic bishop, and being able to help him in various relief parties. He informed us that Mr. Weisberg, Financial Secretary, was also left free, and lived with the Bishop. Sir Shenton Thomas, however, was interned with the remainder of the civilians at Changi, to which camp Gaudard was also eventually taken until he was released for evacuation.

TREATMENT OF CHINESE.

According to Gaudard's information, large numbers of Chinese were rounded up and placed in concentration camps for a few days during which time their houses were inspected by the Japanese. If any signs of pro-Chungking sympathies were found, even a picture of Chiang Kai-Shek being enough, the men were sentenced to be shot.

===== Page 250 =====
This was done after taking them out to sea in boats, the bodies being presumably afterwards thrown into the sea. We were told that about eight thousand Chinese were thus treated.

M. Gaudard's friend informed Mr. Taylor that he had seen personally Chinese being taken onto the boats in batches of four manacled together.

We cannot of course in any way guarantee the truth of the above information, and we had not met Gaudard or his friend before. We can merely say that they appeared to us to be responsible people who would not invent such tales for the sake of sensationalism. We ourselves have a slight corroboration of the story from a remark made by a Japanese civilian attache, whom Mr. Kortright saw frequently, G. Sinsuke Itoh, attached to the F.A. Sec. of the Navy, who was in charge of us for a time during internment and when on parole in Saigon. He was talking to us of the occupation of Singapore and of the anti-Japanese character of the Chinese there. He said that all Chinese who had been guilty of attempting to obstruct the Japanese effort, financially or otherwise, would be "struck down" (making a motion of his hand to his neck). As Mr. Itoh was to all appearances a mild mannered man who always treated us well we attach a fair amount of importance to his statement.

CONDITIONS OF CIVILIANS.

Both Frenchmen agreed that the morale in the concentration camp in Changi prison was high, and that the general treatment by the Japanese was not harsh, but they emphasized that the food situation was very serious. Only rice and salt was provided although a certain amount of other food was allowed to be purchased by the prisoners. As a result, beri-beri had already broken out and they considered that if help were not soon forthcoming numerous deaths would occur.

INDIAN MORALE.

Gaudard further informed us that although many Indians fought well and bravely the Sikhs were notorious for their treachery.

(Signed) J. Kortright.
(Signed) J. Taylor.

===== Page 251 =====
NEWS OF MALAYA

PRISONERS' DIET OF RICE AND VEGETABLES

WORK ON ROAD REPAIR

From our own Correspondent

Chungking, Tuesday. - The first direct news from Malaya since Singapore fell eight months ago was given me in an exclusive interview by Mr. Lishalto, headmaster of the Chinese Middle School in Johore.

"The European prisoners, including civilians, are badly treated," he said. "They are given two small bowls of rice and a tiny ration of vegetables daily, in spite of the fact that they are forced to work hard, mainly repairing roads. Their food is sometimes thrown on the floor.

"Prisoners are not allowed to see friends or to receive reading materials. Some British prisoners who escaped while being taken from Johore to Singapore were recaptured and tortured.

"The food shortage in Malaya has become acute since the Japanese shipped out large quantities. The Chinese community is suffering badly, particularly from malnutrition and consequent diseases.

"Chaolisen, Chairman of the Chinese Overseas Chamber of Commerce, was shot after protracted torture because he refused to work for the Japanese. Other prominent Chinese were executed after they heard their entire families had been tortured to death for refusing to give information as to their whereabouts.

"The natives were originally well treated, but since they have not obtained co-operation the Japanese have changed their policy."

===== Page 252 =====
The Japanese are maintaining only the smallest garrisons, of 100 or 200 soldiers, in most of the large cities.

RELIEF SUPPLIES

"There is still no news of British prisoners in Singapore and Malaya," said Field-Marshal Sir Philip Chetwode at a meeting of the committee of the Red Cross and St. John War Organisation in London yesterday.

Four thousand tons of relief supplies were transported on the "Diplomat" ships from Lourenco Marques, and these had arrived at Singapore. He believed that 1000 tons had been taken out and sent to Hong Kong. The supplies included shoes and special drugs to combat tropical diseases.

===== Page 253 =====
Extract from Monitoring Report Far East October 19, 1942.

Penang Radio (in Malay): at 21.30 hrs on 49.34 metres.

A talk was given which explained that in wartime food and goods were difficult to obtain and necessitated strict economy. Food such as fruit should be grown in order to relieve the situation. Young people must help to grow the food. "Don't waste money by buying non-essentials. Save your money. Take care of your clothes and make the best use of what you have. Don't make more clothes than are needed."

===== Page 254 =====
A talk was given by Tan Chong Hai of the Kuomintang party, praising the reconstruction done by the Japanese after the ruin left by the British "scorched earth" policy. Malayan life is now peaceful and the people are helping to make Malaya self-sufficient. "The most interesting experience I had was discovering that there is now no such thing as caste in Malaya."

"Here is a special announcement: Citizens of Penang: the Japanese authorities have asked you to cooperate in eliminating the Communists from the island. The activities of the local Communist Party have been severely hampered through your cooperation, and the island is practically freed from the Communists. We can look forward to a better Penang, and we take this opportunity of thanking the people of Penang for their help."

===== Page 255 =====
A talk was given on purging communist elements. "We are keenly conscious that the existence of communist elements in our midst is highly detrimental to our programme of national reconstruction. Every sensible person is aware that the final goal of exterminating the communists is not attainable by unaided Governmental effort, but that it needs the concerted efforts of everyone. Everyone knows the nuisance and the evils of the communist elements, and it is necessary for everyone to help to the utmost the campaign to eradicate Communism from among us."

In accordance with the new short-wave system, Tokio will abandon its 25.39 metre wavelength and adopt Hankow's on approximately 49.30 metres.

EXTRACT FROM MONITORING REPORT FAR EAST DATED 1ST OCTOBER.

Penang (in Malay) 21.00 on 49.34 metres:

Extracts from a talk by a Malay official of the Food Department: "We are faced with a great shortage of rice, for Malaya does not grow enough, and the importation of rice is difficult owing to the congestion of the railways and shortage of coal. Do not think the people in Malaya can live without rice. If you do, you are not facing reality. I, an official of the Food Department, urge you to grow rice and other food crops. We must grow rice to escape starvation and so that we need not import it. We have been forced to import rice for many years. Are we not ashamed of this? All our money has gone to other countries for food while we have taken other employment. We have to look after our stomachs now, especially during the early days of the New Order in East Asia. Every Malay house must be surrounded by a garden. By doing this, we Malays need never fear hunger."

Tokyo in Japanese at 19.00 hours Tokyo time on 25.39 metres:

Yesterday, the military administration of the southern regions held a conference at the War Office. Since the southern regions are now regularly administered, it is advisable to establish closer relations among the Japanese military administration in the south in order to build up a solid war structure. Kodama represents Java, and Nagata and Shimada, Malaya and Sumatra.

===== Page 260 =====
The Japanese have shown their respect for Islam by making special arrangements for their employees in Singapore to observe the fast of Ramadan (12 Sept.). They have also allowed the Methodist Church to hold a three-day conference there (20 Sept.).

Singapore school children are being given palm-oil vitamin daily (23 Sept.).

"A new currency exchange system" is to be introduced for Malaya and Sumatra (23 Sept.).

"People's Banks" are to be opened at Kuala Lumpur (24 Sept.).

Revelations of British oppression in Malaya have been made by Tengku Hussein, a direct descendant of the original Sultan of Singapore. He complains that his papers were searched and he was left a whole day at C.I.D. headquarters. Pressure was put on him to use his influence with the Singapore Malays, who at that time were anti-British. He did not expect to survive his treatment, but the capitulation to the Japanese saved him. Members of the Royal Household of Trengganu were also detained and had their papers searched, the reason being that the authorities "feared our continued co-operation with the Japanese army" (25 Sept.).

A Maritime Bureau has been established to control shipping in Borneo (20 Sept.).

EXTRACT from Monitoring Report dated October 5th.

FAR EAST RADIO

Tokyo in Japanese at 19:30 hours Tokyo time on 25.39 metres.

The establishment of the southern regions before, or without winning Greater East Asia, would be unthinkable. Therefore the war may be said to have just begun and the southern regions are still in their infancy. There are Japanese military administrations in all the occupied countries in the south. Like the Philippines and Burma, their future independence is assured, but before they secure their independence they have the important task of building up the Greater East Asia Co-prosperity Sphere, without which independence would be meaningless. For this reason the respective countries are being asked to cooperate.

===== Page 264 =====
Cooperate with Japan in winning the war. The best way in which they can cooperate with, and assist Japan, is to develop their respective countries. In other words, each country should develop its industries and increase the production of goods needed by Japan. For example, Malaya has already increased her rice output, and the raising of two crops yearly is now under consideration.

===== Page 265 =====
EXTRACT from Monitoring Report dated October 5th.

FAR EAST RADIO

Singapore in Malay at 20.50 hours Tokyo time on 25.04 metres:

After the Japanese had captured Taiping, the British started a scorched-earth policy against the people of Malaya. The Japanese treatment of the people of Malaya, on the other hand, left nothing to be desired. The Japanese kindness to the Malays has resulted in complete cooperation between the two races. The Japanese authorities have started working on rubber plantations, and useful commodities such as oil have been extracted from rubber. Mines and factories have also been reopened and production is good. The British neglected food

===== Page 266 =====
Food crops: The Japanese authorities are now trying to make Malaya self-sufficient in foodstuffs. Education is also being promoted, and lower schools have been reopened. Raffles College will soon be reopened. Promising students from all over Malaya and the sons of Sultans are to have refresher courses before being sent out as officials.

===== Page 267 =====
With the resumption of operations by all 18 member corporations of the Shonan Rubber Association, the reconstruction of the rubber industry in Malaya and Sumatra is virtually completed (12 Aug.). High-grade petrol is being procured from it (5 Sept.). Most of the tin mines in Kinta have resumed operations (31 Aug.). Palm oil production has also been resumed, and fisheries are being developed by the Japanese companies (10 Sept.). Light industries, such as the manufacture of soap and matches, are being developed, and unemployment is decreasing (14 Sept.).

The Chinese Association in Malaya is to organise the cultivation of jungle by unemployed Chinese in order to increase food production (19 Aug.). An intensive food production drive is being carried out in Perak, old rubber plantations being cultivated with cereals and vegetables (27, 29 Aug.). Efforts are being made to brighten native life and make them more hard-working and efficient by the provision of entertainment (23 Aug.). Irrigation plans are under discussion.

A Chinese "self-protection corps" has been organised in Kuala Lumpur to co-operate with the authorities in preventing theft (26 Aug.). Postal savings deposited in Malaya and directed by the British to war loans are to be refunded, the funds being borrowed from the Yokohama Specie Bank and Bank of Taiwan (24 Aug.). Singapore Post Office Savings Bank reopened on 2nd September. A new People's Bank was opened on the same day. The Penang People's Treasury has helped over 700 families in less than three months with loans totalling 100,000 dollars (2 Sept.).

A General Railways Bureau is to be established for Malaya and Sumatra (28 Aug.).

A shipping line is operating regularly between Rangoon, Bangkok, Saigon, Batavia, Surabaya and Kuching (5 Sept.).

===== Page 268 =====
(5 Sept.)

The Singapore museum, Botanical Gardens, and Library have been greatly enlarged (4 Sept.).

Japanese newspapers are to be published, and film companies to operate, in Malaya (10 Sept.).

During the celebration of six months of Japanese occupation of Singapore, Chinese and Indian leaders expressed their enthusiasm for the new order. The latter was especially grateful for the work of the Japanese in promoting religious unity among Hindus (15 Aug.). The Overseas Chinese Association of Malaya is planning a goodwill mission to Japan (2 Sept.). A Japanese war memorial in Bukit Timah was to be unveiled on 11th September (9 Sept.). Johore Malayans have contributed to the Japanese memorial there (27 Aug.). The Raffles statue is to be removed, as a "generous tribute," to the museum (7 Sept.).

Japanese interned in Singapore were subjected to every form of inhumanity. Nichi Nichi's correspondent was interned at Port Swettenham in a quarantine station for Indian coolies, and forced to sleep on a hard wooden bed with only a worn-out dirty blanket. Food and water were very bad. In January, the internees were secretly removed to India and confined in the fortress prison in New Delhi, where they were forced to undergo humiliating conditions until the exchange negotiations were concluded. Here there was no protection against heat or cold. Hospital accommodation was insufficient and the British authorities refused to consider requests for sanitary improvements. Food was insufficient and not always fresh, rice always mixed with sand and rice husks which had to be painstakingly removed (1 Sept.).

The Sibu Provincial Office, for the exploitation of raw materials in North-western Borneo, was opened on 8th August.

One in check. Thirdly, when one fasts, one's mind turns to God. Fourthly, fasting teaches self-control and gives one strength to resist temptations. The Japanese can live with a minimum of food and thus do they become tough and thrifty. If you fast, you will save money, besides carrying out God's orders. Fasting thus ensures prosperity in this world and in the next.

AMENDED DISTRIBUTION

[CYPHER] POLITICAL DISTRIBUTION
From: PORTUGUESE EAST AFRICA
FROM LOURENÇO MARQUES TO FOREIGN OFFICE

Acting British Consul-General. D. 12.15 p.m. 29th August, 1942.
No. 184
28th August, 1942 R. 9.20 p.m. 29th August, 1942.

From Sir R. Craigie telegram No. 15.

J.H. Kortright, manager of the Chartered Bank of India, Australia and China at Saigon, states that a Frenchman named Gaudard, who had been for many years manager of a tin mine at Ipoh, informed him that on the outbreak of war with Japan the volunteer corps there was in a state of great disorder. He therefore joined an Indian regiment and fought with it in the retreat as far as Muar, where the commanding officer released him and advised him to make his way to Singapore. After the fall of Singapore he was arrested and imprisoned but later released and managed to secure passage to Saigon with other Frenchmen.

2. Kortright states that after the occupation, the Japanese rounded up and concentrated many thousands of Chinese and then searched their houses. Wherever any "proof" of adherence to Chungking was obtained, even a picture of Chiang Kai-shek was considered proof; the Chinese concerned was condemned to death. Such Chinese were tied together in groups of four and taken out in boats where they were shot, their bodies being thrown overboard. Gaudard stated that 8,000 were so shot.

3. According to Kortright, Mr. Sinsuke Itoh, a Japanese civilian attaché to the Japanese navy, whom he saw frequently, stated before the fall of Singapore that the Japanese would "strike down all Chinese who had been acting against the Japanese".

4. Gaudard told Kortright that the Japanese had killed off most of the Chinese engineers at the tin mines and were finding difficulty in working the mines. Most of the dredgers were sunk. He added that the young rubber trees are almost all ruined owing to the undergrowth being unchecked.

5. Kortright considers Gaudard reliable but does not know the source of his information, for Gaudard cannot have witnessed all, if indeed any, of the executions.

6. Neither Kortright's nor Gaudard's name should be mentioned in any publicity given to this information.

OTP.

===== Page 285 =====
20.47.

MAR ONE: London recent daylight raid on Danzig, according to a commentator in London this evening. It can be compared in some ways with Lancasters' raid on Augsburg in April. It is part of Bomber Command offensive against U-boats which has been going on for a number of months. Air power is now given a reference opportunity striking at U-boats where they cannot dive. The cumulative effect of these raids is delaying construction of U-boats and, in certain instances, destroying them. There are indications, according to information reaching authoritative quarters in London, that Germans are turning from dive-bombers to fighter-bombers because Stukas have not proved all they were thought to be. It is certain, at any rate, that the main constituent of the German air striking force is the long-range bomber and not the dive-bomber.

MAR TWO: An authoritative view is that while the dive-bomber is an extremely formidable form of attack when opposition from anti-aircraft or fighter planes is negligible, it is a fairly easy target when there are anti-aircraft batteries. British fighters and bombers, it is pointed out, have had considerable successes in the Middle East. The fighter-bomber delivers its bombs by use of gunsights. The angle of dive when approaching the target is about forty-five degrees against seventy degrees of the dive bomber but it is considerably easier to manoeuvre if attacked. Reference's first objective at the moment is concentrated on those targets which will best help the Russians. Americans are now represented in councils where "target for tonight" is determined.

ALINEA CGB/MS/IR

MONITORING REPORT

FAR EAST August 4:

TOKIO RADIO (Japanese, 21.00 Tokio time, 25 metres):

For the development of various industries in Malaya and Sumatra, a large labour force will be required. In order to facilitate the mobilization of such a labour force, an organisation which may be called the "Labour Control Association" will shortly be established in Singapore.

The Communications Department has introduced a new scheme whereby ship officers and crews can be promoted to a higher rank merely by undergoing a simple oral examination. Such a scheme is said to have been prompted by a desire to accord better treatment to those already in the Mercantile Marine.

BANGKOK (Thai, 21.30 Tokio time, 49 metres):

The following talk was given: "The fact concerning this new law regarding forced labour is that we Thais must seriously consider whether it is necessary that we should have it enforced or not. The Thais must choose now either to let things go on as they are, when nothing will happen to improve the situation of the shortage of goods, or have things done as they ought to be, to overcome this shortage. However I know I can state on behalf of all Thais that they are willing to assume the burden of doing forced labour. Forced labour must not be considered by Thais as meaning that they have lost part of their personal freedom. On the contrary, Thais must realise that this law is for their good. The purpose of the Government in introducing the new law of forced labour is to make the Thai people into real Thais. The nation must be under the command of our leader and follow the right path, therefore let us unanimously accept the law which the Government is planning to introduce."

===== Page 287 =====
TOKIO RADIO (Japanese 05:00, 25 metres):

The Agricultural Minister, INO, in a public speech at Sendai on food problems in the Co-Prosperity sphere said: "Every effort would be made to perfect the necessary arrangement for the provision of the peoples' necessities of life under wartime conditions. Special attention should be given to the problems of nourishment, with a view to increasing the output of nutritive foods. There was no need to be anxious about this year's harvest. He was convinced that a sufficient supply of foodstuffs could be obtained within the Co-Prosperity sphere."

===== Page 288 =====
SHONAN CITY. LIEUT-GENERAL TOMOYUKI YAMASHITA, COMMANDER IN CHIEF OF JAPANESE FORCES IN MALAYA, IN A STATEMENT ON THE HALF-YEAR ANNIVERSARY OF THE OUTBREAK OF THE GREATER EAST ASIA WAR, THANKED VARIOUS RESIDENT RACES AS WELL AS OFFICIALS OF THE JAPANESE MILITARY ADMINISTRATION FOR THEIR WHOLE-HEARTED SUPPORT WHICH HE SAID HAS CONTRIBUTED IMMENSELY TO THE SWIFT ECONOMIC AND SOCIAL REHABILITATION OF AREAS UNDER JAPANESE OCCUPATION. THOUGH ONLY HALF A YEAR HAS ELAPSED SINCE THE OUTBREAK OF THE GREATER EAST ASIA WAR AND LESS THAN FOUR MONTHS SINCE THE COMPLETION OF JAPANESE MILITARY OPERATIONS IN MALAYA AND SUMATRA, YAMASHITA SAID PEACE AND ORDER HAVE BEEN FIRMLY ESTABLISHED IN THESE AREAS.

WHOLE NATIVE POPULATION HELPS.

THE JAPANESE COMMANDER ATTRIBUTED THE REMARKABLE PROGRESS MADE IN ADMINISTRATIVE WORK IN THIS SHORT PERIOD OF SEVERAL MONTHS FIRSTLY TO THE WHOLE-HEARTED SUPPORT GIVEN TO THE JAPANESE ARMY BY VARIOUS RACES WHO WERE EMANCIPATED FROM ANGLO-AMERICAN IMPERIALISM, AND SECONDLY TO THE EFFICIENCY OF THE JAPANESE MILITARY ADMINISTRATORS WHO HAVE LEFT NO STONE UNTURNED FOR THE WELFARE OF THE INHABITANTS UNDER THEIR JURISDICTION. IN A PRESS INTERVIEW FOLLOWING THE ISSUANCE OF HIS STATEMENT, YAMASHITA SAID WORK ON VARIOUS RECONSTRUCTION PROJECTS THROUGHOUT MALAYA AND SUMATRA HAD BEEN MAKING REMARKABLE STRIDES AND THE SWIFTNESS WITH WHICH REPAIRS WERE BEING EFFECTED HAS SURPASSED ORIGINAL CALCULATIONS.

PERAK RIVER POWER STATION RESTORED.

AS A SPECIFIC INSTANCE, HE CITED THAT THE GIGANTIC POWER STATION ON THE PERAK RIVER WHICH WAS SEVERELY DAMAGED BY RETREATING BRITISH FORCES HAS BEEN RESTORED, WHILE TIN SMELTING WORKS IN VARIOUS PARTS OF MALAYA HAVE RESUMED OPERATIONS.

EXCESS RUBBER NO PROBLEM: OIL FROM RUBBER.

QUESTIONED AS TO WHAT PLANS ARE BEING CONSIDERED FOR THE DISPOSAL OF EXCESSIVE RUBBER OUTPUT, YAMASHITA SAID THERE IS NO NEED FOR ANXIETY ON THAT GROUND AS RUBBER HAS VIRTUALLY UNLIMITED USAGE. HE ADDED THAT JAPANESE RESEARCH EXPERTS RECENTLY CULMINATED EXPERIMENTS TO PRODUCE OIL AND EVEN AVIATION FUEL FROM RAW RUBBER. HE SAID, MOREOVER, THAT WITH THE RESTORATION OF COMMUNICATIONS WITH GERMANY AND ITALY, JAPAN'S ALLIES WILL STAND TO BENEFIT FROM THE HUGE SUPPLIES OF MALAYAN RUBBER.

(MOMI MR. EDMETT COLONIAL OFFICE ALSO)

Malaya.

"Nichi Nichi" recognizes Prince Tong Abdur Rahman of Kedah as the leader of the "United Free Malayans". ("Neue Zürcher Zeitung", Zurich: daily in German: 6th January, 1942).

I.R.B. COL. M.I.5. (INF. I.S.R.B. B.B.C. M.E.W.) 28.3.42. G.D.

===== Page 290 =====
No Japanese Bombs Fell on Malay Quarters in Singapore.

(1650).* No. 7. Tokyo. The 48-year-old Sultan Tunku Sein Sixth, one of the rulers of Singapore Lions Island, wore a shirt and sarong when interviewed by "Yomiuri" correspondent at Shonan Island. He revealed that during the attack on Singapore there were 800 Malays in the garden; the Japanese bombed only the British quarters. "This only served to increase the number of refugees in my garden," the Sultan emphasized, not a single bomb dropped on Malay quarters. The Sultan said his sons Ismael, 7 years, and Ibrahim, age 6, speak a little Japanese and expressed his desire to send them to Tokyo to continue their studies. The dynasty was founded by Sultan Albujalel about 200 years ago and lasted six generations. With the advent of British domination, the power of this dynasty which once controlled the entire island became a dream of the past.

Denial of Japanese Atrocities at Hongkong.

(2201).* No. 8. Shanghai. Bitterly denouncing British claims about Japanese atrocities at Hongkong as "absolutely without foundation," Lieutenant Morito Matsuda, Deputy Japanese Army Spokesman, told a press conference that war prisoners as well as civilians at Hongkong were being accorded excellent treatment. He said the wounded were being given expert care in hospitals and the Japanese military authorities gave the enemy dead careful and most respectful treatment. He revealed that the Japanese Army received a special letter of thanks from the British Commander. Both civilians and soldiers were permitted to receive foodstuffs and read newspapers, Matsuda said, while a hospital had been set up in the internment camp for treatment of the sick. He said British and American doctors were allowed to carry on work while the Japanese provide medical supplies. Matsuda declared these conditions extended to other places where war prisoners were interned. He revealed that prisoners at Shanghai were permitted musical instruments during lunch and dinner hours, have the use of three radios, and are permitted to play baseball and engage in other exercises.

Nanking Celebrates Another Anniversary.

(2211). No. 9. Nanking. Nanking will launch a week's festival tomorrow in celebration of the second anniversary of the return of the seat of Sino Government to Nanking and incidentally the founding of the present Sino National Government. The festival will reach a climax on 30th March—the day of transfer of the capital back to Nanking—with solemn ceremonies at Memorial Hall where the Government and people will renew the pledge to work for peace in China.

French Indo-China's Future.

(2215)* No. 10. Fukuoka. French Indo-China's future depends upon its close cooperation with Japan, Seiki Yano, former Consul-General at Hongkong, declared this afternoon upon arrival by plane from Saigon after an inspection tour of Thailand and French Indo-China. He said economic negotiations between the two countries which are "progressing smoothly" are expected.

Thur. Monson

M.O.I. MR. EDMETT COLONIAL OFFICE ALSO

M.E.W.
TOKIO IN ITALIAN FOR ITALY 2130 14.3.42.

MALAYA - JAPAN'S "NEW ORDER"

THE VICE CHIEF (OF THE MILITARY GOVERNMENT OF SHONAN) WENT ON TO SAY THAT THE JAPANESE GOVERNMENT WILL PROTECT THE LIVES AND PROPERTY AND RELIGIOUS RIGHTS OF THE VARIOUS SULTANS OF MALAYA. THE SAME APPLIES TO OTHER CATEGORIES OF CHINESE, INDIAN, AND OTHER IMMIGRANTS. THIS IS ONLY THE FIRST STEP. AS THEY SHOW GREATER DISPOSITION FOR FRIENDLY COLLABORATION WITH JAPAN THEY WILL GRADUALLY BE ADMITTED INTO SHARING IN ADMINISTRATIVE ACTIVITIES. THE SYSTEM OF FEDERATED STATES WILL BE ABOLISHED FOREVER. (FURTHER SENTENCE ON THIS SUBJECT INAUDIBLE).

ANOTHER IMPORTANT POINT IS THAT THE NUMBER OF PROVINCIAL OFFICIALS WILL BE EXTREMELY SMALL, ONLY A FRACTION OF THOSE WHO FUNCTIONED UNDER BRITISH RULE. FINANCIALLY THE COUNTRY WILL BE COMPLETELY SELF-CONTAINED FROM THE ECONOMIC VIEW. THE EXPLOITATION OF TIN, BAUXITE, AND OTHER NATURAL RICHES WILL BE CONTROLLED BY A FEDERATION FORMED TO GIVE AN INCREASED RHYTHM TO INDUSTRY. ENEMY PROPERTY WILL PASS UNDER THE ADMINISTRATION OF THIS FEDERATION. ULTIMATE CONTROL WILL BE WITH THE GOVERNMENT. FOR THE TIME BEING THE CURRENCY IN MALAYA WILL BE THAT AUTHORISED BY THE JAPANESE MILITARY AUTHORITIES OR THE OLD CURRENCY OF THE STRAITS. TO PREPARE THE PEOPLE TO TAKE THEIR PLACE IN THE FOREFRONT OF MALAYAN RECONSTRUCTION, THE JAPANESE AUTHORITIES HAVE DECIDED TO OPEN A LARGE EDUCATIONAL INSTITUTE IN KUALA LUMPUR. UNDER THE JAPANESE, THE COUNTRY WILL HAVE A VERY DIFFERENT FUTURE FROM ITS EXISTENCE UNDER THE ENGLISH.

CORRECTION SECOND PARA. FIRST WORD OF THIRD LINE

FUNCTIONED.

===== Page 293 =====
JAPANESE PLANS FOR THE CONTROL OF MALAYA'S ADMINISTRATION AND RAW MATERIALS.

TRANSOCEAN IN ENGLISH (FOM) 1508 14.3.42.

TOKYO: THE DEPUTY CHIEF OF THE JAPANESE MILITARY ADMINISTRATION IN THE MALAY PENINSULA, COLONEL WATAMBE, GAVE INFORMATION AT HIS PRESS CONFERENCE IN SINGAPORE REGARDING PLANS FOR THE FUTURE ORGANISATION OF MALAYA. HE SAID THE MAIN OBJECT WOULD BE TO OBTAIN CONTROL OF ALL RAW MATERIALS PRODUCED THERE WHICH COULD BE UTILIZED FOR THE CONDUCT OF WAR. THE ADMINISTRATION, WHICH WILL BE UNDER THE STRICT SUPERVISION OF THE JAPANESE MILITARY AUTHORITIES, WOULD BE AS LITTLE COMPLICATED AS POSSIBLE. THE INTENTION PREVAILED OF UTILISING TO THE LARGEST POSSIBLE EXTENT ALL AVAILABLE LABOUR POWER AND THE SYSTEM HITHERTO ADOPTED BY THE BRITISH WOULD IN GENERAL BE RETAINED.

AT A LATER DATE THE ADMINISTRATION COULD BE REORGANISED CONFORMABLY WITH JAPANESE PRINCIPLES. ALTHOUGH SUBORDINATED TO JAPANESE MILITARY AUTHORITIES, THE ADMINISTRATION WOULD APPOINT EXPERIENCED CIVILIANS TO HIGHER POSTS. IT WAS HOPED TO REDUCE THE TOTAL NUMBER OF OFFICIALS TO ABOUT ONE TENTH OF WHAT IT WAS UNDER BRITISH RULE.

COLONEL WATAMBE WENT ON TO SAY THAT A SIMILAR SYSTEM WAS PLANNED FOR SUMATRA. BANKS WOULD BE ENCOURAGED TO REPORT AS SOON AS POSSIBLE AND WOULD BE ASSISTED IN PROMOTING PRIVATE ENTERPRISE ALSO BY THE CHINESE.

THE COLONEL ANNOUNCED THAT IN MALAYA THE PRODUCTION OF RUBBER AND TIN WOULD FOR THE TIME BEING BE RESTRICTED SINCE IT WAS FAR IN EXCESS OF JAPAN'S REQUIREMENTS. THE PRODUCTION OF TIN, BAUXITE, AND OTHER MINERAL ORES WOULD BE SUPERVISED BY JAPANESE EXPERTS GROUPED IN A SPECIAL ORGANISATION, WHILE RUBBER PLANTATIONS WOULD PROVISIONALLY BE MANAGED BY JAPANESE INDUSTRIAL UNDERTAKINGS.

A SPECIAL SCHOOL WOULD BE OPENED AT KUALA LUMPUR FOR TRAINING OFFICIALS FOR JAPANESE ADMINISTRATION, BUT THIS SCHOOL WOULD ALSO RECEIVE MALAY, CHINESE, AND INDIAN STUDENTS DESIROUS OF FINDING SUITABLE EMPLOYMENT LATER. ALTHOUGH JAPANESE SKILLED WORKERS AND EXPERTS WOULD BE SENT TO MALAYA, THERE WAS NO INTENTION OF ENCOURAGING LARGE SCALE EMIGRATION OF JAPANESE AS IN THE CASE OF MANCHOUKUO.

===== Page 294 =====
I ASSURE YOU
By Bill Greig

Indian Quislings set up in Malaya

JAPAN is installing Indian “Quisling” administrators in the territories in Malaya occupied by her troops. At the same time, she is promising these areas complete independence within the “New Asiatic Order.”

The use of Indian Quislings is part of the Japanese attempt to win over discontented elements in India with the promise that an India cooperating with the Axis-Japan group would become a great nation working out her own destiny.

It will take strong British propaganda—and perhaps more than propaganda—to counteract this move, and there is no sign of it yet.

Japanese wireless stations are now telling the Indians hour after hour that the British are so occupied in Libya that they will not be able to defend India.
